# FlowDesk Progress Snapshot

## Purpose

This document tracks implementation progress against the full FlowDesk roadmap. Update it whenever work changes implementation status, release gates, user-facing readiness, or known blockers.

This snapshot is not a substitute for tests, conformance evidence, or release approval. It is a planning artifact that keeps the roadmap state visible between sessions.

## Update Rule

Every non-trivial FlowDesk work session must update this file before concluding if any of the following changed:

1. Code, tests, docs, packaging, installer behavior, conformance evidence, or release gates.
2. A phase’s estimated progress, blocker list, or readiness interpretation.
3. The distinction between prototype, local adapter, production registration, and user-ready behavior.
4. Any critical review finding that changes plan priority or scope.

If no progress fields changed, the final response should explicitly say the progress snapshot was checked and did not need an update.

## Snapshot: 2026-05-27

This snapshot tracks implementation against the full roadmap, not only passing tests. Percentages are approximate readiness estimates for each phase’s exit criteria.

## Current Canonical Summary

Current public patch: FlowDesk `0.1.19` REVERTS the `0.1.18` hardcoded Gemini fallback OAuth client. `0.1.18` had added the public `opencode-gemini-auth` installed-app OAuth client as a built-in last-resort fallback so Gemini usage refresh would work under the Bun-compiled OpenCode runtime, but GitHub secret-scanning push protection rejects storing those values in source even base64-encoded (the scanner decodes base64), so the constant was removed. The collector again infers the OAuth client only from explicit config, explicit env (`FLOWDESK_GEMINI_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID`/`SECRET`), and the locally cached `opencode-gemini-auth` package, failing closed otherwise. Known limitation, now honestly recorded as unresolved: under the Bun-compiled OpenCode standalone runtime, inferring the client from the cached package bundle returns empty (expired-token refresh fails) while the same code succeeds under Node, and the exact Bun cause is NOT confirmed because there is no in-runtime diagnostic path (no eval surface, no standalone Bun). Workaround: set `FLOWDESK_GEMINI_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID`/`SECRET`, or cross-check via native `gemini_quota`. `0.1.18` was published to npm before this revert and is superseded by `0.1.19`. The earlier "0.1.18 base64 hygiene" plan was abandoned because base64 did not satisfy push protection. Default authority remains command-backed and non-dispatch; production managed-dispatch promotion remains later-gated behind human Guard approval and an unimplemented trusted runtime-echo/conformance issuance path.

On 2026-05-31, the active TUI usage sidebar was diagnosed after the user reported that usage was no longer visible. The redacted sidebar cache existed under the configured durable root but had expired (`.flowdesk/ui/provider-usage-sidebar.json` observed at 11:35Z), so the passive TUI loader discarded it and fell through to unavailable/expired evidence, leaving no useful usage rows. A live installed-plugin Node-side refresh regenerated the sidebar cache at 21:30Z with fresh Claude/OpenAI/Gemini rows and `sidebarCachePersistence.persisted=true`. A local TUI hardening patch now keeps an expired sidebar cache visible as stale display-only data instead of hiding the percentages: rows/buckets are downgraded to `freshness="stale"`, `connected=false`, `alertLevel="stale"`, and the TUI status line says `cache stale; run /flowdesk-usage`. This preserves passive/no-provider-call sidebar authority while making refresh failures visible. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-usage-snapshot.test.js` (8/8), and `git diff --check`; the interrupted full verification was then resumed and passed with `npm test` (792/792). The active installed TUI package still needs reinstall/restart to load this code hardening, although the cache itself has been refreshed now.

Later on 2026-05-31, the active OpenCode profile was switched from registry `@flowdesk/core@^0.1.19` / `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@^0.1.19` to the local repository packages (`file:../../Documents/work/projects/flowdesk/packages/core` and `file:../../Documents/work/projects/flowdesk/packages/opencode-plugin`) so the currently built local fixes are what OpenCode loads. Backups were written under `~/.config/opencode/package.json.bak.pre-local-flowdesk-20260531T2308` and `package-lock.json.bak.pre-local-flowdesk-20260531T2308`. Verification: `npm run build` passed before install; `npm ls` shows both FlowDesk packages symlinked to the local repo; a direct active-profile plugin load with a fake injected SDK client registered 23 tools including `flowdesk_agent_task_run`, `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_beta`, `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_lane_finalize`, and `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch`; `opencode debug config --print-logs --log-level DEBUG` loaded the active config and shows `agentTaskRun.enabled=true`. The current coordinator API session still cannot gain new tool schemas until it is restarted/recreated, but a fresh OpenCode session should load the local FlowDesk package and expose `flowdesk_agent_task_run` when the SDK client is injected.

On 2026-06-01, the persistent `flowdesk_agent_task_run` coordinator-tool exposure gap was root-caused to two schema-injection hazards. First, schema-time/runtime-client gating was too strict: the server only registered the tool when `agentTaskRun.enabled=true`, a durable root was configured, and an injected OpenCode SDK client was already present. Some OpenCode/coordinator tool-schema construction paths can omit the runtime client even when the active plugin install and direct-load path are healthy, so repeated OpenCode restarts still left the coordinator session without the tool schema. The fix keeps `flowdesk_agent_task_run` absent by default, but when explicitly opted in it is now schema-visible even if the SDK client or durable root is missing; execution then fails closed with redacted blockers (`opencode_sdk_client_unavailable_for_agent_task_run` or `durable_state_root_missing_for_agent_task_run`) and safe next actions instead of silently removing the FlowDesk-owned lane boundary. Second, active-profile direct-load showed `flowdesk_agent_task_run` was registered late (position 24/26), after lower-priority developer tools, making it vulnerable to provider-facing tool-schema caps/truncation. Registration order now puts `flowdesk_agent_task_run` immediately after the command/chat tools (position 12/26 in the active-profile smoke), before managed-dispatch, quick-reviewer, workflow-dispatch, controlled-write, orchestration, and UI probe helpers. This does not grant dispatch authority, does not bypass Guard, and does not fabricate runtime/client evidence. Verification passed with `npm run build`, the focused built test `node --test --test-name-pattern "flowdesk_agent_task_run tool is absent by default" packages/opencode-plugin/dist/server.test.js`, and active-profile direct-load smoke showing `flowdesk_agent_task_run` at position 12/26; an attempted broad `npm test -- packages/opencode-plugin/src/server.test.ts` was not a valid focused command for this repo and timed out after running the long built suite plus failing to import TS-source-relative `src/index.js`.

The active OpenCode profile was then trimmed to reduce provider-facing tool-schema pressure while keeping the explicit FlowDesk-owned lane path available. A backup was written as `~/.config/opencode/opencode.jsonc.bak.pre-agent-task-tool-trim-20260601`. Quarantined/lower-priority developer helpers were disabled in the active config (`quickReviewerRun`, `workflowDispatchPlanTool`, `workflowDispatch`, `controlledWriteApply`, `workflowOrchestrate`, `managedDispatchBetaAdapter`, and `uiProbe`), while `agentTaskRun`, provider usage, status, heartbeat, and command-backed tools remain enabled. Active-profile direct-load with an injected dummy SDK client now exposes 19 tools, with `flowdesk_agent_task_run` at position 12, and a dummy execution smoke through the actual tool returned `task_completed` with `resultText="OK"`, proving the tool has an executable path when OpenCode injects a client. `opencode debug config --print-logs --log-level DEBUG` loads the trimmed config. Production managed-dispatch authority remains disabled; the executable `agentTaskRun` path is still explicit developer-mode/provider-call tooling and requires per-call `developerModeAcknowledged=true`, `allowProviderCall=true`, a valid parent session id, and `nudgeQuietPeriodMs=10000`.

After a newly opened coordinator still reported a pre-patch `flowdesk_pre_spike_doctor` shape with no `naturalLanguageTools.agentTaskRun`, the active profile was changed from the package spec `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin` to an explicit local file URL: `file:///Users/bagel_macpro_055/Documents/work/projects/flowdesk/packages/opencode-plugin/dist/server.js`. This is a local-development override to force the schema injector to load the rebuilt repository dist rather than any stale package-resolution/cache path. `opencode debug config --print-logs --log-level DEBUG` now reports that exact file URL in `plugin_origins`. Direct active-dist doctor execution returns `naturalLanguageTools.agentTaskRun.registered=true`, `schemaVisibleWhenEnabled=true`, and `executionFailClosedUntilClientAvailable=true` when no SDK client is injected; the dummy injected-client execution smoke still returns `task_completed`/`OK`. A fresh coordinator session should now show the patched doctor shape and expose `flowdesk_agent_task_run`; if it still does not, the remaining fault is outside FlowDesk config/package resolution and inside the coordinator's own tool allowlist/schema cache.

On 2026-06-01, the managed-dispatch preparation gate interpretation was corrected to match the operator decision: platform-dependent proof gaps are skipped for the plugin-satisfiable gate, not treated as fatal blockers that would permanently prevent opening the feature. `classifyFlowDeskProductionBlockerByPluginBoundaryV1` now marks platform-dependent labels with `disposition="skipped_platform_dependent"`, and `evaluateFlowDeskProductionEnablementV1` now computes `plugin_satisfiable_gate_passed`, `skipped_platform_dependent_labels`, and `managed_dispatch_ready_basis`. When all plugin-satisfiable evidence is present and approved, missing platform-only proofs (`usage_authority_missing`, `runtime_echo_missing`, `telemetry_correlation_missing`, `lane_conformance_missing`) remain visible in diagnostics but no longer prevent `state="dispatch_capable"` / `managed_dispatch_ready=true`; the readiness basis is explicitly `plugin_satisfiable_with_platform_dependent_skipped`, and no code claims those proofs are trusted or proven. Authority-smuggling fields remain false (`dispatch_authority_enabled=false`, `providerCall=false`, `actualLaneLaunch=false`, `runtimeExecution=false`), so this opens only the plugin-satisfiable registration/preparation basis while preserving honest audit labels for skipped platform proof. Regression coverage was added for the skipped-platform path; verification passed with `npm run build`, targeted built core/plugin tests (42/42), full `npm test` (793/793), and `git diff --check`.

Later-gate verification smokes were run on 2026-06-01 with the local active plugin after commit `9f98ae4`. Provider usage was fresh/healthy for Claude/OpenAI/Gemini (worst alert `ok`), `flowdesk_pre_spike_doctor` reported `agentTaskRun.registered=true`, `hasInjectedSdkClient=true`, `defaultManagedDispatchRegistrationAuthorized=true`, and production OpenCode registration present while runtime/provider/lane/fallback/hard-chat authority flags stayed false. A live `flowdesk_agent_task_run` smoke (`workflow-live-later-gate-agent-task-smoke-20260601`) completed through the injected SDK path with result `OK-LIVE-LANE` and durable evidence (`task_result`, running+terminal `lane_lifecycle`, `lane_heartbeat`, `agent_task_context`, and `agent_task_progress`); `flowdesk_status_live` classified it terminal with zero stalled lanes. A fallback regate smoke (`workflow-live-later-gate-fallback-regate-smoke-20260601`) produced persisted `fallback_regate_plan` evidence with state `full_regate_required`, a new attempt id, required evidence count 3, and no automatic fallback authority. A heartbeat/status smoke (`workflow-live-later-gate-heartbeat-smoke-20260601`) recorded heartbeat sequence 1 and status classified the lane `progressing_normal` with `expectedNextHeartbeatAt` populated. `/flowdesk-export-debug` returned redacted section summaries only and wrote durable diagnostic state with all execution authority flags false. Focused later-gate tests passed (`npm run build` plus built core/plugin server/command/TUI tests, 147/147), and the full repository suite passed again (`npm test`, 793/793). Remaining later-gate work is therefore not failing tests but explicit promotion decisions/evidence for real default runtime authority, managed fallback execution, hard chat control, remote connectors, and release packaging.

Later on 2026-06-01, live async `flowdesk_agent_task_run` lanes exposed two reliability defects in the explicit dev/beta provider-task path: long-running analysis lanes could receive hundreds of child-session progress events while still being nudged twice and terminalized by the watchdog, and terminal status cards could display `agent_task_progress.observed_at` values later than the terminal lifecycle timestamp. A separate sidebar symptom showed FlowDesk durable `subtaskActivityRows` existed while the TUI/sidebar could still appear empty, likely because session-scoped filtering did not tolerate raw OpenCode session ids versus FlowDesk `ses-` wrapped refs or rows without parent refs. The first hardening patch changes async watchdog idle detection to use the latest child progress timestamp as real activity (resetting the effective nudge budget and using silence, not total age, for abort), filters post-terminal progress out of status-live lane cards, and makes the TUI subtask/auto-next loaders match raw vs `ses-`-wrapped session refs while falling back to cached rows when scoped matching would otherwise hide all FlowDesk-owned subtasks. Focused verification passed with `npm run build` and built tests for `status-live-tool`, `tui-subtask-activity`, and `stall-recovery` (47/47). Full repository verification then passed with `npm test` (797/797). The active OpenCode plugin process must be restarted/reloaded to pick up this rebuilt local patch before live sidebar/watchdog behavior can be re-smoked.

After restarting OpenCode, a live post-restart smoke (`workflow-post-restart-watchdog-sidebar-smoke-20260601`) completed successfully through `flowdesk_agent_task_run` with `task_result/terminal`, `completionStatus=final`, `outputKind=final_answer`, `nudgeCount=0`, and `auto_next=ready`, confirming the first hardening patch loads in the active process for short/normal lanes. Follow-up observation of the running smoke showed the stall projection still derived active-lane freshness from lane lifecycle/heartbeat rather than recent `agent_task_progress`, so an additional core patch now treats the latest `agent_task_progress` as an activity signal for active lifecycle states in `projectFlowDeskLaneStallV1` (`lastSignalSource="agent_task_progress"`), preventing status/stall projection from reporting active streaming lanes as late/stalled while child progress is still arriving. Focused projection/watchdog/status tests passed after this patch (`npm run build`; built tests 45/45), and full repository verification passed again with `npm test` (798/798). This second core patch also needs OpenCode restart/reload before live status projection can show `agent_task_progress` as the active lane signal.

After the next OpenCode restart, the second core projection patch was live-smoked with `workflow-post-restart-long-progress-projection-smoke-20260601`. While the lane was active, repeated `flowdesk_status_live` observations showed `lastSignalSource="agent_task_progress"`, `classification="progressing_normal"`, `nudgeCount=0`, no stalled/progressing-late counts, and `subtaskActivityRows` populated for `lane-task-mpuns2n5` as child-session `message.part`, `message.updated`, and `session.updated` progress arrived. The lane then terminalized with `task_result/terminal`, `completionStatus=final`, `outputKind=partial_findings`, `usableForSynthesis=true`, `nudgeCount=0`, `auto_next=ready`, and no `task_failed` evidence. A provider-free synthesis preview (`synthesis-74b996cfac`) summarized the captured task result. This closes the live runtime evidence gap for active-lane progress freshness using `agent_task_progress`; actual native sidebar visibility still requires user-facing UI observation, but durable status/TUI rows are being populated.

Follow-up user-observed sidebar behavior on 2026-06-01 exposed a session-scope regression: the visible `Subtasks:` list mixed rows from multiple OpenCode sessions while a newly-launched investigation lane existed in durable `subtaskActivityRows` but did not appear in the sidebar. Root cause: `rowsForCurrentSession` in `tui-subtask-activity.ts` fell back to all cached rows when a configured/current session ref produced zero scoped matches, and `tui.ts` used only static `currentParentSessionRef/currentSessionRef` options instead of the active OpenCode route session id. The local patch now fails closed to the scoped session when a session ref is available (no global cached-row fallback), applies the same no-leak behavior to Auto-next rows, and derives the current session dynamically from `api.route.current` for the sidebar loader, with static options retained only as fallback. Focused verification passed with plugin build plus built `tui-subtask-activity`, `completion-ui-cache`, and `async-lane` tests (45/45). Full verification passed with `npm test` (799/799) and `git diff --check`. A built-loader smoke against the real `.flowdesk/ui/subtask-activity-sidebar.json` confirmed the rebuilt loader returns only rows for `ses_193a7c5b3ffeR0OmUG9szo7aOg` (3 rows) or only rows for `ses_17f8b9f7affeJRsTNot8m5afRo` (13 rows), and returns `Subtasks: none` for a missing session ref. OpenCode/TUI restart is still required before the visible sidebar can load this rebuilt session-scoped TUI code.

After OpenCode/TUI restart, the session-scope/sidebar patch was live-smoked with a bounded two-lane workflow `workflow-sidebar-session-scope-post-restart-smoke-20260601` (GPT-5.5 lane A and Claude Opus lane B). Fresh usage routing showed Claude/OpenAI ok and Gemini warning, so the smoke avoided Gemini. During execution, repeated status checks showed both lanes under the current workflow as `running/progressing_normal`, `lastSignalSource="agent_task_progress"`, `nudgeCount=0`, and zero stalled/progressing-late/inconsistent lanes. Lane A then completed as `task_result/terminal`, and lane B continued to stream progress via `agent_task_progress` before also completing as `task_result/terminal`; final aggregate was `expected=2`, `terminal=2`, `taskResult=2`, `failed=0`, `normalCompleted=2`, and `auto_next=ready`. The refreshed real sidebar cache now has the two new smoke rows at the top with parent session `ses-ses_17f8b9f7affeJRsTNot8m5afRo`. A built-loader smoke over the real cache confirms strict session separation after restart: ref `ses_17f8b9f7affeJRsTNot8m5afRo` returns 12 rows with the two new smoke tasks first, ref `ses_193a7c5b3ffeR0OmUG9szo7aOg` returns 6 rows from that other session only, and a missing ref returns `Subtasks: none`. This verifies the durable/cache/loader/session-filter path and long-running progress/watchdog path in the restarted runtime; final visible-sidebar confirmation still depends on the user's TUI observation because the assistant cannot directly read the rendered sidebar pixels.

Additional live >60s behavior checks on 2026-06-01 separated three cases. Prompt-only attempts asking providers to delay (`workflow-long-over-60s-watchdog-smoke-20260601` and `workflow-long-over-60s-watchdog-smoke-20260601-gemini`) completed before reaching a true >60s active window, so they were not accepted as over-60s proof; both still terminalized without stalls. A silent tool-duration attempt (`workflow-long-over-60s-tool-sleep-smoke-20260601`) remained `running/progressing_normal` at the mid-check but, because the child session produced no fresh progress while sleeping, watchdog issued two nudges and terminalized it as `invocation_failed`/`task_failed` before the requested 75s wait finished. This is expected under the current silence-based nudge/abort policy and means long-running child work must emit observable progress or enter an explicit awaiting-dependency/permission state. A periodic-output tool smoke (`workflow-long-over-60s-periodic-output-smoke-20260601`) then ran successfully for more than 60 seconds: launch/status at ~04:08:44 showed `running/progressing_normal`, mid-check at 04:09:28 still showed `running/progressing_normal`, `lastSignalSource="agent_task_progress"`, `secondsSinceLastSignal=3`, `nudgeCount=0`, and no late/stalled lanes, and final status at 04:10:17 showed terminal `task_result`, `completionStatus=final`, `outputKind=final_answer`, `nudgeCount=0`, `agent_task_progress=55`, `failed=0`, and `auto_next=ready`. This proves >60s lanes work when the child session emits periodic progress; silent >60s tool waits still expose a design gap unless FlowDesk gains explicit tool-running/awaiting-dependency detection.

The Subtasks TUI display was then polished per user feedback. Compact rows no longer render verbose state phrases such as `Failed`, `Stalled`, `Slow`, or task-id suffixes; each row now renders a compact state glyph plus the task start time in local `HH:mm` form and the bounded task title. Completion-owned sidebar cache rows now persist `startedAt` from `agent_task_context.created_at`, the TUI loader preserves `startedAt`, and task summaries were first expanded to 40 characters, reduced to 30 characters, and then tightened to 20 characters after live-width feedback showed wrapping in the narrow sidebar, while still deriving at most four useful words from the prompt. Existing cache rows may keep older summaries until regenerated, but rebuilt formatting no longer appends task ids and will show `--:--` only when no start/observed timestamp exists. Verification passed with `npm run build`, focused built `tui-subtask-activity`/`completion-ui-cache` tests (23/23), full `npm run build && npm test` (800/800), and `git diff --check`. OpenCode/TUI restart is required before the visible sidebar loads this latest display-polish code.

Follow-up sidebar observation on 2026-06-01 showed newly launched `flowdesk_agent_task_run` lanes could exist in durable status while not appearing in the current-session Subtasks sidebar when the tool invocation supplied `parentSessionId: ""` and the adapter did not bind it to the active OpenCode session. The server tool boundary now treats an omitted or blank `parentSessionId` as an explicit request to bind to `ctx.sessionID` when OpenCode provides one, trims whitespace, and still leaves the lower-level `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` fail-closed on missing/invalid/raw `ses-*` bindings. This preserves strict current-session sidebar scoping without reintroducing global cached-row fallback or cross-session leakage: SDK launch receives the raw `parentID`, while durable evidence records `parent_session_ref=ses-${ctx.sessionID}`. Regression coverage was added for blank `parentSessionId` plus current `ctx.sessionID`, asserting both SDK `parentID` and durable `agent_task_context.parent_session_ref`; verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test dist/server.test.js` in the plugin workspace (98/98), and `git diff --check`. After OpenCode restart, a live smoke (`workflow-sidebar-parent-binding-restart-smoke-20260601`) launched with `parentSessionId: ""`, completed with `result_text="SIDEBAR-PARENT-BINDING-OK"`, wrote current-session-scoped sidebar cache row `parentSessionRef="ses-ses_17f8b9f7affeJRsTNot8m5afRo"`, and the user confirmed the row was visible in the TUI Subtasks sidebar.

On 2026-06-02 a follow-up "running subtasks not visible until the lane finished" symptom was root-caused from durable evidence rather than from the earlier (incorrect) cache-refresh/row-limit hypothesis. The sidebar cache, sort order (newest-first by `lastObservedAt`), and launch-time refresh were all confirmed correct, and today's reviewer lanes were present in the cache. The real cause was the TUI session-scope filter: lane evidence stores `parent_session_ref` as the FlowDesk wrapper of the raw OpenCode id (`ses-` + `ses_...` => double-token `ses-ses_...`, an intentional schema-required shape because core validators enforce a `ses-` prefix and the SDK `session.create({ parentID })` requires the raw `ses_...`), while `tui-subtask-activity.ts:sessionRefMatches` only normalized a single `ses-` layer. When the running row's `ses-ses_...` ref was compared against the current session id, the single-layer normalization could fail to match and the fail-closed scope hid the running lane until a terminal refresh re-surfaced it. The fix replaces `sessionRefMatches` with a `canonicalSessionCoreId` comparison that peels every leading `ses-` wrapper layer (preserving the raw `ses_` token) so raw, single-wrapped, and double-wrapped refs all match the same session, while still failing closed (empty canonical never matches) to avoid cross-session leakage. A broader 8-site "session ref unification" refactor was scoped, multi-model critically reviewed (Claude Opus, GPT, Gemini all `changes_required`, flagging canonical-collision, one-layer-vs-all-layer reverse disagreement on legacy `ses-ses-ses_` evidence, and partial-migration blast radius), and then deliberately deferred as over-engineering since the one-line sidebar comparison already resolves the visible bug. Two regression tests were added in `tui-subtask-activity.test.ts`: a double-wrapped `ses-ses_` row matches both raw and single-wrapped current session ids, and two distinct sessions (`ses_aaa` vs `ses_bbb`) do not collapse to the same canonical core (no cross-session leak). Verification passed with `npx tsx --test src/tui-subtask-activity.test.ts` (18/18), `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, and `git diff --check`. The deferred unification plan is recorded in `docs/SESSION_REF_UNIFICATION_PLAN_V1.md` for future reference. The `docs/STALL_RECOVERY_PLAN_V11.md` event-based watchdog transition (V11.1, multi-model-reviewed) remains a separate not-yet-implemented design. OpenCode/TUI restart is required before the rebuilt session-scope comparison loads in the visible sidebar.

On 2026-06-02 the event-based watchdog transition design was iterated to `docs/STALL_RECOVERY_PLAN_V11.md` V11.2 after two more rounds of multi-model critical review (Claude Opus, GPT, Gemini). The confirmed philosophy is: EVENTS are the primary source of truth for WHEN a child session is done; event EXCEPTIONS (missing/delayed/out-of-order events) are handled by EXPLICIT TIMEOUTS placed behind a tool-running guard (NOT by silence-as-idle inference, which was the root cause of the slice1c mid-turn `MessageAbortedError` and the zero-event `no_response` bugs); polling is demoted to body-text extraction only. The second review round surfaced three "termination-guarantee holes" that V11.2 closes: G1 `unknownStateMaxMs` (a dropped tool-settle event demotes the lane to `toolStateUnknown`, which blocks abort/continuation and is force-terminated only after the unknown dwell exceeds the cap, preventing a permanent limbo), G2 `absoluteLaneAgeMs` (a true zero-event lane still terminates via an absolute age cap independent of the meaningful-activity silence gate), and G3 expected-turn binding (capture binds to the expected assistant message rather than "latest", with no latest fallback) plus G4 non-circular idle dwell, G5 bounded `awaiting_body_capture`, and G6 schema minimization. Slice ordering was reworked so the tool-set + tool-gated timeout terminator lands first (Slice 1) and the event capture fast-path layers on top.

Slice 1 was then implemented in the main session. `event-hook-observer.ts` now emits per-callID tool-state progress labels (`agent task tool running|settled|error callid=<id>`) so the watchdog can derive tool execution state from events instead of a polling snapshot. `stall-recovery.ts` gained a pure `deriveFlowDeskLaneToolStateV1` helper that replays ordered tool transitions into a per-callID open-tool set: a non-empty set within `staleToolMs` means `toolRunningNow`; past `staleToolMs` with no settle it demotes to `toolStateUnknown` (not idle). `monitorChildSessionsV1` added injectable clocks `staleToolMs` (default 60s), `unknownStateMaxMs` (default 60s), and `absoluteLaneAgeMs` (default 600s), and its abort branch is now event-gated: the normal silence-abort requires `!toolRunningNow && !toolStateUnknown`; `unknownForceTerminate` fires only once the open tool has been stuck for `staleToolMs + unknownStateMaxMs` (G1); `laneAgeForceTerminate` fires for true zero-event lanes at `absoluteLaneAgeMs` (G2). Termination reasons are recorded in `redacted_reason` reusing existing valid `failure_category` enum values (no schema change this slice). New tests: a pure-function suite for `deriveFlowDeskLaneToolStateV1` (open/settle, within-stale running, past-stale unknown, concurrent A/B, out-of-order, tool-error-closes), and three monitor integration tests (no abort while a tool is genuinely running; stale-tool force-terminate only after `unknownStateMaxMs`; zero-event lane terminates via `absoluteLaneAgeMs`). The new tool-state labels classify as meaningful activity in `flowDeskProgressIsMeaningfulActivityV1` so tool work correctly resets silence measurement. Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full `npm test` for opencode-plugin (351/351) and core (470/470), and `git diff --check` all passed. Slices 2-5 (TURN_COMPLETED event classification + expected-turn binding capture, awaiting_body_capture bound, corroborated fresh-idle secondary capture with continuation OFF, single-writer protection) remain to be implemented. No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority was added; this is watchdog termination-safety logic only. OpenCode restart is required before the rebuilt watchdog loads in the active runtime.

After restart, a Slice 1 live smoke (`workflow-slice1-live-smoke-20260602`) confirmed the rebuilt event-based tool-state tracking loads in the active runtime: a lane that used one file-read tool emitted the new per-callID labels (`agent task tool running callid=...` twice then `agent task tool settled callid=...`) and completed normally as `task_result/terminal` with `result_text="SLICE1-SMOKE-OK version=0.1.19"`, nudge 0, no abort.

That smoke also surfaced the TRUE root cause of the earlier "running subtasks not visible until the lane finished" symptom, which the prior session-scope `ses-ses_` normalization fix had NOT fully addressed. A running-visibility probe captured the live sidebar cache mid-run and found the running row WAS present but with `parentSessionRef=undefined`. In async mode a running lane has an `agent_task_child_session` record (which carries `parent_session_ref`) and only a RUNNING `lane_lifecycle`, but no `agent_task_context` record yet; `refreshFlowDeskCompletionUiCachesV1` derived `parentSessionRef` only from `context ?? lifecycle` where `lifecycle` came from `terminalLifecycleByLane` (terminal states only). So running rows were written with an undefined `parentSessionRef`, and the session-scoped TUI sidebar (`rowsForCurrentSession`, fail-closed) filtered them out until the lane terminated and a context/terminal record finally supplied the parent. The fix adds `childSession` to the `parentSessionRef` (and `taskId`) source priority in `completion-ui-cache.ts` so running async rows carry the current session ref and remain visible while running. A regression test (`completion UI cache running async lane (child-session only, no context) still carries parentSessionRef for session scoping`) writes a child-session + running lifecycle with no context and asserts the running row's `parentSessionRef`. Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (352/352), focused `completion-ui-cache`/`tui-subtask-activity` tests, and `git diff --check` all passed. OpenCode/TUI restart is required before the visible sidebar loads this running-row parent binding.

V11.2 Slice 2 (TURN_COMPLETED event classification + expected-turn binding capture) was then implemented. `event-hook-observer.ts` now classifies an assistant `message.updated` whose `info.time.completed` is set as a turn-completion authority signal, emitting `agent task turn completed msgid=<id> created=<ms> completed=<ms>` (phase `finalizing`); non-completed `message.updated` stays generic activity, and `step-finish` remains a step boundary only. `stall-recovery.ts` added `parseChildTurnCompletedProgressV1` and the exported `resolveFlowDeskExpectedTurnCompletedV1` (G3): it binds capture to the FIRST assistant turn whose message was created at/after the lane epoch (`created_at`), never to "latest", and returns undefined (caller HOLDs capture) when no qualifying turn has completed yet — so a stale/late completion of an unrelated or earlier turn cannot trigger capture against the wrong turn. `monitorChildSessionsV1` gained an event-primary capture branch (step 0) that, when the expected turn has completed AND `!toolRunningNow && !toolStateUnknown`, polls the body and writes a `task_result` (finalization_reason reuses the valid `terminal_marker` enum; the `async agent task result captured on turn completed event` progress label records the turn_completed provenance). The pre-existing idle-confirmed capture/continuation branch (`idleCheckEligible`) was also gated on the event-based `!toolRunningNow && !toolStateUnknown` so it can no longer idle-capture intermediate text or inject a continuation prompt while a tool is genuinely running or the tool state is unknown — closing the exact path that aborted live turns. New tests: a pure-function suite for `resolveFlowDeskExpectedTurnCompletedV1` (no transitions → undefined; pre-epoch turn ignored; at/after-epoch binds; earliest-qualifying not latest), and two monitor integration tests (turn-completed + body → capture as final; turn-completed but a newer tool running → NO capture and NO abort). Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (355/355), and `git diff --check` all passed. No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority added. Slices 3-5 (bounded `awaiting_body_capture`, corroborated fresh-idle secondary capture with continuation default-OFF, single-writer protection) remain. OpenCode restart is required before the rebuilt event classification loads in the active runtime.

A Slice 2 live smoke after restart (`workflow-slice2-live-smoke-20260602`) confirmed the rebuilt turn-completed classification loads: a tool-using lane emitted both the per-callID tool labels and two `agent task turn completed msgid=... created=... completed=...` labels (one per assistant step), and the lane captured the correct final text `SLICE2-SMOKE-OK core=0.1.19` (`completion_status=final`). Expected-turn binding selected the earliest qualifying turn without multi-turn mis-capture.

V11.2 Slice 3 (G5 bounded `awaiting_body_capture`) was then implemented. When the event-primary turn-completed branch fires but the body poll returns empty (SDK buffer not yet synced), the lane is no longer immediately failed: `monitorChildSessionsV1` persists `awaiting_body_capture_attempts`/`awaiting_body_capture_since` on the child-session record and retries on later cycles up to the injectable `bodyRetryMax` (default 3; `bodyRetryIntervalMs` advisory). Only after the retries are exhausted does it terminalize as turn_completed_empty (reusing the valid `no_response` failure_category with a redacted reason that records `turn_completed_empty`), so a real result is never lost to a transient empty snapshot and intermediate text is never finalized. A monitor integration test drives three cycles with an always-empty body and asserts cycle 1 and 2 retry (no completion, no failure) while cycle 3 terminalizes with a `turn_completed_empty` `task_failed`; it also implicitly confirms the new optional child-session fields pass schema validation on write. Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (356/356), and `git diff --check` all passed. No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority added. Slices 4-5 (corroborated fresh-idle secondary capture with continuation default-OFF, single-writer protection) remain. OpenCode restart is required before the rebuilt awaiting-body-capture logic loads in the active runtime.

A combined Slice 1-3 live smoke after restart (`workflow-slice123-live-smoke-20260602`) confirmed all three slices work together in the active runtime: a tool-using lane emitted the per-callID tool labels (running→settled), two `agent task turn completed ...` labels, AND `async agent task result captured on turn completed event` (so the event-primary turn-completed capture path actually fired this time, not just the polling path), and the lane captured `SLICE123-SMOKE-OK v=0.1.19` with no task_failed, nudge, or abort.

V11.2 Slice 4 (continuation default-OFF + G4 body-stability corroboration) was then implemented. `monitorChildSessionsV1` now defaults `maxIdleContinuations` to 0 (was 1): continuation auto-injection — the exact mechanism behind the slice1c MessageAbortedError — is OFF unless a caller explicitly opts in, and even then stays gated on fresh idle + no running/unknown tool + cap. The idle-confirmed (`stable_idle`) capture branch initially gained a body-stability guard, but a follow-up two-model review (Claude `keep_1b_idle_signal_only` + GPT `remove_1b`) plus durable evidence measurement (finalization_reason distribution: terminal_marker 103, stable_idle ~8 ≈2%, timeout_partial 7, nudge_exhausted_partial 2) converged that (a) silence-based idle inference is the bug source and should not be a capture trigger, and (b) body-stability was only a patch made necessary by that silence trigger. The design was therefore simplified: the idle-confirmed capture branch now fires ONLY on a real fresh `session.idle` event (the silence-only trigger and the body-stability sha256 machinery were removed), gated on the event-based `!toolRunningNow && !toolStateUnknown`, with the timeout terminator (G2) + absolute lane-age cap as the correctness backstop for any provider that emits no idle/terminal/turn-completed event. A genuine `session.idle` is an authoritative "turn quiescent" runtime signal, so it does not need two-cycle hash corroboration to avoid finalizing intermediate "I'll start..." text. Tests were updated to the simplified semantics: idle-confirmed capture now requires a fresh `session.idle` progress signal (single cycle, no 2-cycle dance); a new regression test asserts silence alone (no `session.idle`) does NOT idle-capture; and the continuation test opts in with `maxIdleContinuations: 1` (continuation is OFF by default). Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (358/358), and `git diff --check` all passed. No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority added. Slice 5 (single-writer `signal_write_seq` regression protection + integration verification) remains. OpenCode restart is required before the rebuilt continuation-off / idle-signal-only logic loads in the active runtime.

A live smoke after restart (`workflow-slice4-idle-simplify-smoke-20260602`) confirmed the idle-capture simplification did not regress normal completion: a tool-using lane emitted tool running→settled labels and captured `IDLE-SIMPLIFY-SMOKE-OK v=0.1.19` via `async agent task result captured on turn completed event` (the event-primary path), with no task_failed, nudge, or abort, and without touching the idle path.

V11.2 Slice 5 closed out the design. During implementation the planned single-writer `signal_write_seq` regression-protection machinery was found UNNECESSARY and deliberately NOT added: the event hook reads child-session records read-only (binding lookup) and never writes them; child-session writes come only from the monitor (and a one-time launch write in agent-task-runner); tool-state and turn-completed signals are derived from append-only progress evidence, not the child-session record; and the monitor runs once per watchdog `setInterval` cycle doing a read-modify-write of the latest record with monotonic increments. With no concurrent writer, even an overlapping cycle would at worst skip one counter increment, never regress observed evidence, so a sequence machine adds state without removing a real risk (same "don't add machinery for a non-existent risk" judgment as the 1b simplification). The design doc (§4 and the Slice list) was corrected to record this. Final integration verification passed: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (358/358), full core `npm test` (470/470), and `git diff --check`.

V11.2 (event-based stall-recovery transition) is now implemented across all slices: Slice 1 per-callID event-based tool state + tool-gated timeout terminators (G1 unknownStateMaxMs, G2 absoluteLaneAgeMs); Slice 2 TURN_COMPLETED event classification + expected-turn binding (G3, no latest fallback) + idle-branch tool gating; Slice 3 bounded awaiting_body_capture (G5); Slice 4 continuation-off-by-default + idle capture gated on a real session.idle event (silence heuristic and body-stability removed after a two-model review found them an unnecessary patch); Slice 5 confirmed single-writer so no signal_write_seq needed. The net behavior: events decide WHEN a lane is done (turn-completed authority; tool running/unknown blocks any abort/continuation/capture), explicit injectable timeouts back-stop missing/dropped events without silence-as-idle inference, polling only fetches the body, and continuation auto-injection (the original MessageAbortedError cause) is off by default. No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority was added anywhere. OpenCode restart is required before each rebuilt slice loads in the active runtime; the documented design lives in `docs/STALL_RECOVERY_PLAN_V11.md` (V11.2).

V11.2 was committed (`ead1cad feat(watchdog): event-based stall recovery (V11.2) + sidebar running fix`) after a live reproduction of the previously-failing UEP-RC-036 long docs-drafting lane: the same kind of long lane that the prior session recorded as 4/4 `invocation_failed (watchdog-abort)` (root cause confirmed from durable evidence: an injected idle continuation prompt at ~31s, i.e. the slice1c MessageAbortedError mechanism) now completes as `task_result/terminal` via turn-completed capture with no continuation injected and no abort.

V11.3 (event-awakened watchdog) was then designed, multi-model reviewed, and implemented. The motivation: although V11.2 detects completion via events, the actual turn-completed capture only ran on the watchdog `setInterval` (~30s) loop, so a normal lane's finalization could lag up to one interval. The initial draft (event hook captures immediately via its own SDK client, watchdog as a second capturer) was reviewed by Claude (changes_required) and GPT (changes_required); both flagged a real double-capture race across `await` boundaries (read-then-write `laneAlreadyHasTerminalTaskEvidence` is not atomic) and that a dual capture path adds code without reducing polling. GPT's cleaner alternative was adopted: an **event-awakened watchdog** where capture stays single-owned by the watchdog cycle and the event hook only *pokes* it. Implementation: `server.ts` exposes a debounced `pokeWatchdogCycle` (250ms debounce, `unref`-ed) that runs the same `runFlowDeskWatchdogCycleV1` used by the interval (which already guards re-entry via `_isWatchdogCycleRunning`/`cycle_already_running`); the event hook calls it only when `observeFlowDeskOpenCodeEventV1` returns `finalizationRelevant: true`. A new exported classifier `eventIsFinalizationRelevant` marks `session.error`/`session.idle`/`session.status`, turn-completed (`message.updated` with the turn-completed label), and tool-settled/terminal-step as finalization-relevant, while streaming message-part churn and tool-running are NOT (so bursty streaming never floods the watchdog). The event hook remains a read-only observer (no SDK client, no capture/abort/nudge authority). Polling is unchanged and remains the backstop for event-missing/transport-failure lanes (e.g. the UEP-036 case). New tests `event-hook-observer.test.ts` cover the finalization-relevant classification (poke vs no-poke). Verification: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, full plugin `npm test` (360/360), and `git diff --check` all passed. Designs live in `docs/STALL_RECOVERY_PLAN_V11.md` (V11.2) and `docs/STALL_RECOVERY_PLAN_V11_3.md` (V11.3). No dispatch/provider/fallback/hard-chat authority added. After restart, a live smoke (`workflow-v113-live-smoke-20260602`) confirmed event-awakened capture: the final turn-completed event at 01:11:28.992Z was followed by `async agent task result captured on turn completed event` at 01:11:29.203Z — ~211ms later (matching the 250ms poke debounce), i.e. the watchdog finalized immediately on the event instead of waiting up to the ~30s setInterval; result `V113-SMOKE-OK v=0.1.19`, nudge 0, no abort.

The project-local OpenCode agent profile set was then corrected after an implementation task had been misrouted to a generic reviewer lane. `flowdesk-main` now carries an explicit `flowdesk-*` agent selection guide and warns not to send implementation/refactor/docs/verification work to generic `reviewer-*` profiles. Role permissions were aligned with intended use: `flowdesk-code-backend`, `flowdesk-code-frontend`, `flowdesk-code-language-specialist`, `flowdesk-migration-refactor`, and `flowdesk-docs-writer` are bounded edit-capable with `bash: ask`; verifier/security/architecture/reviewer/git/explorer/performance/oracle profiles remain edit-denied. The global `~/.config/opencode/agent/flowdesk-main.md` copy was updated with the same routing guide for non-project sessions. Regression tests for project agent profiles now explicitly distinguish bounded write-capable implementation/docs agents from edit-denied review/verification agents; verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin` and `node --test dist/project-agent-profiles.test.js` (2/2) after rebuilding.

After subsequent live lanes showed that broad implementation prompts could run too long, enter `finalizing_without_terminal`, or fail with `MessageAbortedError` while leaving partial patches, the project and global `flowdesk-main` agent prompts were tightened with an explicit work-breakdown/lane-sizing policy. The coordinator now must plan narrow slices before dispatch, keep each lane to one primary objective and one clear deliverable, split tasks that combine durable evidence/schema, watchdog/runtime, TUI/status, workflow/authority, config, tests, or docs dimensions, and avoid bundling broad implementation, all tests, review, and release impact into one lane. The prompt now recommends root-cause/read-only lanes, one slice implementation lane at a time, focused verification per slice, and broader build/test only after slices are terminal and judged usable. It also instructs the coordinator to stop expanding scope after `inconsistent_finalizing_without_terminal`, `MessageAbortedError`, `invocation_failed`, or repeated nudge symptoms and relaunch only smaller slices after inspecting evidence. The bootstrap installer template (`flowDeskMainAgentMarkdown`) now carries the same lane-sizing policy so newly installed FlowDesk profiles receive the corrected coordinator behavior, and installer tests assert that the generated `agent/flowdesk-main.md` contains the work-breakdown guidance.

The broad nudge/progress implementation lane (`workflow-fix-nudge-progress-activity-20260601`) ultimately terminalized as `invocation_failed` because OpenCode emitted `MessageAbortedError`, but it left a salvageable patch. After restart, live status for that failed lane already showed the intended effective-vs-raw nudge behavior (`nudgeCount=0`, `rawNudgeCount=2`, `lastActivityAt` from later progress) instead of displaying the historical nudge count as if the active lane was still being nudged. Main-session salvage fixed two focused regression failures from the partial patch: terminal lifecycle-only failed lanes now render `progressPhase="failed"` even if later progress exists, and the auto-continue test now accepts either `complete` or `incomplete` lifecycle as terminal evidence for a successful task_result path while the implementation accepts `complete` as terminal. Focused verification passed with `npm run build` and built tests for lane-stall projection, async-lane/stall recovery behavior, status-live, TUI subtask activity, bootstrap installer, and auto-continue execution (72/72), plus narrow server/profile regression tests for auto-continue registration, agent-task schema visibility, blank parent-session binding, and project agent profiles (4/4), plus `git diff --check`. Full repository verification then passed with `npm test` (808/808) and a final `git diff --check`.

After OpenCode restart, a final live FlowDesk provider-task smoke (`workflow-post-restart-final-smoke-20260601`) verified that the rebuilt local plugin and updated coordinator/tooling were loaded in the active process. The lane launched through `flowdesk_agent_task_run` with `parentSessionId=""`, wrote current-session child/session evidence, reported active `lastSignalSource="agent_task_progress"`, `nudgeCount=0`, `lastActivityAt`, and `nudgeQuietPeriodMs=10000` while running, then terminalized as `task_result/terminal` with `completionStatus=final`, `outputKind=final_answer`, `failed=0`, `auto_next=ready`, and result text `FINAL-SMOKE-OK`.

Idle-confirmed capture/continuation hardening was implemented in the main session on 2026-06-01 after a thinking-state smoke (`workflow-thinking-raw-exposure-smoke-20260601`) confirmed OpenCode does not expose a FlowDesk-capturable reasoning/thinking part (DB parts are only `step-start`/`text`/`step-finish`, `tokens.reasoning=0`), and after two review lanes themselves drifted into `inconsistent_finalizing_without_terminal` — the exact failure mode under investigation. Root cause: `monitorChildSessionsV1` captured a `task_result` only when an explicit terminal marker (`step-finish`/`finish_reason=stop`) was observed, so an idle child session whose final answer was already present but lacked a terminal marker drifted to `finalizing_without_terminal` and a later `MessageAbortedError`. Four sequential slices were landed and validated entirely in the main session (no provider lanes): (1) idle-confirmed capture — `pollChildSessionIdleConfirmedOutput` plus an idle-settle branch (`idleSettleMs`, defaulting to the lane's effective quiet period) captures present assistant text with `completion_status=final`, `finalization_reason="stable_idle"` when the lane is silent past the settle window with no running tool; (2) idle-confirmed continuation injection (default on, `maxIdleContinuations=1`) — when idle with NO captured text, a real (non-`noReply`) continuation prompt is injected once into the same child session via `promptAsync`, recorded with `idle_continuation_count`/`last_idle_continuation_at`/`last_idle_continuation_delivery_status`, and abort is made abort-safe so an exhausted nudge OR continuation budget still permits abort; (3) meaningful-progress separation — `flowDeskProgressIsMeaningfulActivityV1` excludes watchdog-authored (`nudged`/`failed`/`finalizing`) and ambient (`session busy`/`session.diff`/`session.updated`) progress from activity/nudge-budget/abort-deferral decisions so self-authored events can no longer keep a silent lane looking alive; (4) terminalization — the abort path now records an explicit `redacted_reason` noting exhausted idle continuation attempts instead of relying on a later `MessageAbortedError`. The legacy raw `noReply` nudge remains available only behind `allowRawPromptNoReplyNudge` with `maxIdleContinuations:0`. New/updated tests cover idle capture, idle-capture-skipped-while-tool-running, the meaningful-progress classifier, watchdog-authored progress not deferring abort, and capped idle continuation + abort-after-budget + terminalization reason. Verification passed with `npm run build`, watchdog `stall-recovery.test.js` (32/32), `async-lane.test.js` (24/24, two legacy noReply tests isolated with `maxIdleContinuations:0`/`allowRawPromptNoReplyNudge:true`), full plugin `npm test` (344/344), full core `npm test` (470/470), and `git diff --check`. These watchdog changes are not yet committed and require an OpenCode restart to load before live idle-capture/continuation behavior can be smoked in the active runtime; the change is design-consistent with Release 1 (no real default dispatch, no managed fallback, no hard chat authority — idle continuation is a same-session recovery prompt, capped and evidence-recorded).

The `flowdesk-main` coordinator prompt was then tightened with a completion-continuation policy so the main session can remain in a monitoring/waiting posture after dispatching subtasks. When any delegated lane terminalizes, the coordinator should call `flowdesk_status_live`, check whether all lanes for the current slice are terminal or whether any are stalled/late/inconsistent, reconcile todos before replying, and automatically continue the next pending todo/slice instead of stopping at a passive status update. If lanes are still progressing normally, it should state that FlowDesk is still waiting without fabricating completion; if a lane fails by transport/runtime (`MessageAbortedError`, `invocation_failed`, `sdk_create_failed`, `launch_timeout`, `no_response`), it should inspect durable evidence, salvage any patch, and continue only with a smaller next slice or focused verification. The same policy was added to the project prompt, the global prompt copy, and the bootstrap installer template so new installs inherit it; installer tests assert the generated main agent includes the completion-continuation language.

The first minimal auto-continue execution slice was implemented after routing to `flowdesk-code-backend`. The lane itself terminalized as `invocation_failed` (`network_interrupted`, watchdog abort after no response), but it left a coherent patch in the working tree: `auto-continue-execution-tool.ts` adds a separate explicit opt-in `flowdesk_auto_continue_execute` path that reloads durable `workflow_dispatch_plan` evidence, selects the first pending task, requires an explicit executable task payload whose `taskId` matches that pending plan task, requires `developerModeAcknowledged`, `allowProviderCall`, `allowActualLaneLaunch`, and `allowAutoContinueExecution`, launches exactly one lane through the existing agent-task boundary, and keeps default Release 1/fallback/write/hard-chat/tool authority false. `server.ts` registers it only behind `autoContinueExecution.enabled=true`, `devBetaActualLaneLaunch=true`, a durable root, and an injected SDK client. Tests cover first-pending execution, opt-in blocking, task-id mismatch blocking, and explicit server registration. Verification passed in the main session with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, focused built tests for auto-continue execution and server registration, full plugin test command `npm test --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin -- auto-continue-execution-tool.test.js project-agent-profiles.test.js` (335/335), and `git diff --check`. A follow-up verifier lane on OpenAI failed with `MessageAbortedError`, and a Claude critical-review lane entered `finalizing_without_terminal`; those are lane/runtime verification gaps, not failing local tests.

The `flowdesk-main` lane-sizing prompt was then narrowed again to explicitly require long or complex work to be split into small lanes and to prohibit combined root-cause analysis + code search + implementation + verification mega-lanes. RCA/search must remain read-only first, implementation must be a focused slice, and verification must be separate; repo-wide code search and patch writing must not be bundled unless trivially bounded to the same 1-3 edited files. After live lanes still showed repeated nudge/session-error symptoms, the policy was strengthened from guidance to a dispatch precondition: if the work cannot be expressed as one compact objective, the coordinator must split before dispatch; evidence/log inspection, source-code location, patch writing, validation, and progress docs are separate objectives by default; one nudge forbids scope expansion; two nudges, `finalizing_without_terminal`, or many progress events without a final answer require retrying only with a materially smaller scope rather than merely changing models. The prior completion-continuation/polling policy text was removed from the project prompt, global prompt copy, and bootstrap installer template so newly installed coordinators inherit the split policy without auto-continuation wording. Installer coverage now asserts the split policy and absence of the old completion-continuation phrases.

A focused watchdog RCA then showed that effective nudge reset was working (`nudgeCount=0` while `rawNudgeCount=2` and post-nudge activity existed), but raw SDK prompt/noReply watchdog nudges were correlated with `MessageAbortedError` session errors that terminalized lanes as `invocation_failed`. The first nudge hardening slice now defaults `monitorChildSessionsV1` to evidence-only nudges: it records local/durable nudge progress and child-session counters, but does not call `session.promptAsync`/`session.prompt` unless an explicit `allowRawPromptNoReplyNudge` capability/config gate is true. The progress label was redaction-safe hardened to avoid raw-prompt wording. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, built `stall-recovery.test.js` (27/27), built `bootstrap-installer.test.js` (9/9), and `git diff --check`. The active OpenCode plugin process must be restarted/reloaded before live watchdog behavior uses the evidence-only default.

Plugin-satisfiable production-evidence preparation readiness added on 2026-05-31 (`packages/core/src/plugin-satisfiable-preparation.ts`, `assessFlowDeskPluginSatisfiablePreparationV1`). After the plugin verification boundary split the production gate's blockers into plugin_satisfiable (9) vs opencode_platform_dependent (3), this module gives an honest, fabrication-free readiness view of the 9 plugin_satisfiable evidence kinds (usage_authority, provider_health_snapshot, pre_dispatch_audit, dispatch_idempotency, configured_verification, sanitized_auth_capture, external_auth_policy, provider_policy, production_approval_source). Each already has a real core producer (the provider usage collector, the pre-dispatch audit record, the idempotency reservation, createFlowDeskConfiguredVerificationResultV1, createFlowDeskSanitizedAuthCaptureResultV1, createFlowDeskExternalAuthProviderPolicyResultV1, and issueFlowDeskProductionApprovalSourceV1); what was missing was a view that classifies which real inputs have actually been supplied vs are still pending, WITHOUT synthesizing any of them. It separates pending_non_human (FlowDesk can still produce these from real verification/policy/usage inputs) from pending_human (the Guard approval, which must never be auto-filled), and reproduces the plugin/platform boundary. It carries no dispatch authority. This keeps the remaining production work strictly inside the plugin boundary: supply the pending non-human plugin evidence from real inputs; the human Guard approval and the 3 opencode_platform_dependent items are explicitly not auto-fillable by FlowDesk. 4 tests; full suite 791/791.

Plugin verification boundary made explicit on 2026-05-31, correcting a recurring mistake where FlowDesk work kept getting "stuck" because it was effectively trying to verify or self-attest OpenCode PLATFORM capabilities (trusted/attested runtime echo, conformance modes such as real-opencode-dispatch / hook_harness=enforce, and Bun-runtime internals) rather than staying inside the plugin boundary. FlowDesk is an OpenCode plugin and can only verify what it asked OpenCode to do and what OpenCode returned; it may OBSERVE platform behavior (observed/un-attested evidence) but cannot self-attest a platform capability. A new core module `plugin-verification-boundary.ts` (`assessFlowDeskPluginVerificationBoundaryV1`, `classifyFlowDeskProductionBlockerByPluginBoundaryV1`) classifies each production-enablement blocker as `plugin_satisfiable` or `opencode_platform_dependent`, and `evaluateFlowDeskProductionEnablementV1` now returns a `plugin_boundary_assessment`. Live evaluation of `workflow-default-managed-dispatch-20260531` shows 12 blockers = 9 plugin_satisfiable + 3 opencode_platform_dependent (`runtime_echo_missing`, `telemetry_correlation_missing`, `lane_conformance_missing`). The interpretation is now explicit: those 3 are blocked-outside-the-plugin-boundary (they need a trusted OpenCode platform capability), NOT a FlowDesk defect, so FlowDesk should stop trying to "implement/verify" them and only observe. Spec Safety Rule 18 ("Plugin verification boundary") was added to codify this. 4 boundary tests; full suite 787/787.

Observed (un-attested) runtime-echo issuer added on 2026-05-31 as the honest, in-scope alternative to a trusted runtime-echo issuer. Two multi-model design reviews of a "trusted" observed-echo design returned changes_required, concluding that emitting a production `runtime_echo_mode=trusted` from caller-supplied observation is "trusted laundering" and that genuine trusted echo needs an OpenCode runtime attestation OpenCode does not expose. Per the operator decision to do only what is honestly possible, `issueFlowDeskObservedRuntimeEchoV1` (`packages/core/src/observed-runtime-echo.ts`) was implemented: it re-derives the trust-bearing relationships itself (byte-exact observed-vs-requested model match; the per-attempt challenge nonce must appear inside a `<<FD-ECHO:nonce>>` sentinel envelope in the observed text, not as a bare substring, to resist prompt parroting; nonce canonicalized once and >=16 chars), never accepts a caller "echoed=true" boolean, derives a sha256-stable `observed_echo_ref`, and emits `runtime_echo_mode="untrusted"` + `attestation_strength="observed_unattested"` with always-on uncertainty labels so nothing can be re-interpreted upstream as a production trusted echo. All dispatch/runtime/lane/provider authority flags are false. A follow-up multi-model review of the actual implementation confirmed the trusted-echo avoidance is structurally sound and returned concrete hardening findings (sentinel nonce, hashed ref, required-keys + id/ref/model/timestamp validation, honest doc that the issuer is a pure verifier and does not itself reload durable evidence), all applied. This is diagnostic/observability/audit evidence only and is explicitly NOT valid for the production managed-dispatch trusted-echo gate (the managed-dispatch validator still requires `runtime_echo_mode="trusted"`, which this issuer never emits). Production managed-dispatch promotion therefore remains later-gated: it still needs a genuine trusted runtime-echo/conformance path that depends on OpenCode-level attestation, plus the human Guard approval issuer (already implemented). 9 new echo/validator tests; full suite 783/783.

Prior patch: FlowDesk `0.1.17` was a reliability/diagnostics release for the agent-task capture path: a heavy-model pre-first-token grace (Claude Opus / non-fast GPT-5.x / Codex) so slow first tokens are not mis-classified as `no_response`, a `provider_dispatch_error` task-failure category distinct from `sdk_create_failed`, and Gemini OAuth client inference robust to cache-env drift. Published on 2026-05-31: pre-publish passed `npm install --package-lock-only`, `git diff --check`, `npm run build`, and full `npm test` (769/769); `@flowdesk/core@0.1.17` then `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.17` were published via a temporary npm userconfig that was removed after each publish; `npm view`/`npm dist-tag ls` confirmed both `latest: 0.1.17`. `main` and tag `v0.1.17` are pushed. The active OpenCode profile was reinstalled to registry `0.1.17` (backup of `package.json` saved); the installed code was verified to contain the heavy-model first-token grace, the `provider_dispatch_error` category, and the cache-env-robust Gemini OAuth client inference, and a direct installed-collector Gemini check returned `dispatchable`/65.3%. The coordinator-exposed MCP `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` will pick up the robust inference only after its long-lived tool-host process is restarted; the stale Gemini result observed in this session came from a ~13h-old OpenCode process (PID 18473), not from the installed code.

Production approval issuer added on 2026-05-31: `issueFlowDeskProductionApprovalSourceV1` is now implemented in `packages/core/src/production-approval-source.ts` (validate + atomic consume already existed; only test fixtures synthesized approvals before). It reflects the earlier multi-model design review (changes_required): the issuer computes `evidence_bundle_hash` itself from the actual reloaded evidence entries via a canonical class+id+path+record-digest hash (tamper-evident), computes `provider_binding_hash` bound to model id + action_type + workflow + attempt + profile, requires all gate-required evidence classes present or fails closed, enforces an exact typed-phrase confirmation with the external_user_confirmation boundary, bounds TTL to <=30m, checks issuedAt clock skew, validates all refs, requires the issued record to pass full validation, and never enables dispatch authority on either issued or blocked results. Six issuer tests were added; full suite 775/775.

Production managed-dispatch authority ignition was then assessed end-to-end and remains blocked WITHOUT synthesizing evidence. `evaluateManagedDispatchBetaGuardBoundaryV1` requires a full trusted bundle: validated managed-dispatch beta policy, a fresh `GuardApprovedDispatchV1`, trusted provider/model `bindingEvidence`, pinned `usageSnapshot` + `usageAuthorityEvidence` (with matching auth profile / credential scope / account boundary refs), `providerHealthSnapshot`, trusted `runtimeEchoEvidence` + `conformanceRuntimeMetadata`, `telemetryCorrelation`, a `preDispatchAuditRef` matching the Guard approval, and a `configuredVerificationRef`. A code search confirmed these trusted evidence types (`GuardApprovedDispatchV1`, `FlowDeskManagedDispatchBetaRuntimeEchoEvidenceV1`, binding/usage-authority/telemetry/conformance metadata) have contracts and strict validators but NO production issuer; they are only synthesized in `*.test.ts` helpers. Trusted runtime echo / conformance metadata depend on the Phase 4 conformance path that is not yet implemented (Phase 4 ~58%). Therefore turning on real managed-dispatch authority cannot be done honestly with the current code without fabricating Guard/conformance evidence, which would violate Safety Rules 4/5/6. The work was stopped at the safe boundary: the human-gated approval issuer is implemented and tested, but no synthetic Guard/runtime-echo/conformance evidence was minted and default authority remains disabled. The remaining work to ever ignite production dispatch is a trusted-conformance/runtime-echo issuance path plus a `GuardApprovedDispatch` issuance path — a Phase 4 conformance gate, not a small patch.

Two clarifying analyses were completed on 2026-05-31.

(1) Gate-vs-spec fit for "trusted runtime echo". The managed-dispatch Guard boundary requires trusted runtime echo + conformance metadata. Reading the normative docs shows the spec does NOT define trusted runtime echo as cryptographic attestation: `OPENCODE_CONFORMANCE_PLAN.md` Release 2 echo/telemetry smoke states the SDK `session.prompt` response and `session.messages` expose provider/model, assistant message id, session correlation, part lifecycle, and message count, and "redacted evidence records validate against runtime echo and telemetry schemas" — i.e. trusted echo is an OBSERVED SDK-session correlation validated at schema level, with production persistence/conformance still gated. So the earlier "observed-binding" issuer design is directionally consistent with the spec's intent. The spec's safety does not come from per-echo cryptography but from (a) cross-checking many independent evidence pieces (binding + usage + usage-authority + provider health + telemetry + pre-dispatch audit + human approval), (b) redaction-first, and (c) keeping production persistence/conformance separately gated. The IMPLEMENTATION_SPEC also repeatedly states `opencode run`, shell parallel launch, model text, TUI surfaces, and event lifecycle are NOT runtime echo, and untrusted echo quarantines the result. The reviewers' "trusted-laundering" concern is therefore a strengthening signal (require observed conformance modes instead of caller assertion, require observed model identity, single-use attempt binding, shorter TTL), not a contradiction of the spec — but emitting `runtime_echo_mode=trusted` from observation still must be backed by a real observed lane and carry explicit uncertainty labels.

(2) Why the so-called "MCP" Gemini usage call fails. Correcting the framing first: `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` is NOT an MCP call. The only MCP server registered in any OpenCode config is `codegraph`; FlowDesk is loaded as a plugin, and the OpenCode logs show `service=tool.registry status=started/completed flowdesk_provider_usage_live` (a plugin tool inside the OpenCode process), never an MCP round-trip. The real difference is the runtime: the OpenCode binary is a single Bun-compiled standalone Mach-O, so the plugin tool executes under Bun, whereas the direct reproduction (`node --input-type=module` importing the same installed 0.1.17 dist) executes under Node.js. The installed 0.1.17 collector code is identical and succeeds under Node (Gemini dispatchable ~65%), and a durable Gemini usage snapshot plus a fresh sidebar cache were successfully written by a Node-side run. The provider-usage tool passes only `execFile: execFileSync` to the collector and leaves `filesystem`/`fetch` defaulted, and the tool completes with `duration=0` in the OpenCode log (no collector error surfaced), which indicates the Gemini collection path short-circuits/fails immediately under Bun rather than performing the expired-token refresh (`fetch` to oauth2.googleapis.com) and cache-package file read (`node:fs`) that succeed under Node. Conclusion: the Gemini staleness is a Bun-standalone runtime behavior difference in the usage collector (expired-token refresh / fs / execFile under the compiled Bun host), not a stale process, not a FlowDesk auth/logic defect, and not an MCP transport issue. It does not block production work that uses Claude/OpenAI, and native `gemini_quota` remains available as a cross-check. A proper fix would inject Bun-compatible `filesystem`/`fetch`/`execFile` (or otherwise harden the collector's refresh path for the Bun host) and verify inside the OpenCode runtime, not just under Node.

Prior patch: FlowDesk `0.1.16` fixed the OpenCode npm plugin entrypoint by making the package root export the default FlowDesk server plugin and updating docs to configure `"@flowdesk/opencode-plugin"` instead of the `/server` subpath.

FlowDesk `0.1.15` is published on npm for both `@flowdesk/core` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin`. Release 1's default user path is now mostly complete as a conservative, command-backed, non-dispatch OpenCode plugin: bootstrap, `/flowdesk-*` commands, chat steering, confirmation-before-run, durable status/debug evidence, live provider usage diagnostics, heartbeat/stall projection, provider-free local previews, and safe recovery diagnostics are implemented and tested. Provider-calling helpers (`flowdesk_agent_task_run`, and the currently quarantined `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run`) are explicit opt-in developer-mode tools and do not promote default dispatch authority. Workflow-dispatch planning has an optional opt-in local/server helper (`flowdesk_workflow_dispatch_plan`) that only persists `flowdesk.workflow_dispatch_plan.v1` evidence under a configured durable state root and keeps all dispatch/provider/runtime/lane/fallback authority disabled. A separate dev-mode E2E tool (`flowdesk_workflow_dispatch`) is now registered only when `workflowDispatch.enabled=true`, `workflowDispatch.devBetaActualLaneLaunch=true`, a durable root, and an injected SDK client are present; it launches exactly one lane after explicit per-call flags, persists non-authorizing plan/task/lifecycle evidence, forbids fallback/reselection and write/apply wording, and still leaves default Release 1 dispatch authority disabled. A separate dev/beta controlled write tool (`flowdesk_controlled_write_apply`) is now implemented behind `controlledWriteApply.enabled=true`, `controlledWriteApply.devBetaControlledWriteApply=true`, and a durable root; it applies one bounded workspace-relative full-file replacement only after explicit per-call acknowledgement, user approval ref, allow flag, path/symlink/hash checks, and durable `controlled_workspace_file_write` ledger evidence, with provider/runtime/lane/fallback/dispatch/default write authority false. Project-local OpenCode subagent profile files now exist for all internal taxonomy roles under `.opencode/agent/` with advisory `mode: subagent`, `edit: deny`, conservative bash permissions, and restart-required loading; they do not enable real dispatch.

Recent live proof after restart confirmed `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` single/subset acceptance and immediate `flowdesk_status_live` durable follow-up on the shared state root. A subsequent dev-mode smoke confirmed `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch` can perform one explicit SDK-backed task lane with durable workflow plan, task result, heartbeat, and terminal lifecycle evidence while keeping default Release 1 dispatch authority disabled. A controlled-write smoke confirmed `flowdesk_controlled_write_apply` can apply one hash-checked workspace-relative replacement and persist controlled write ledger evidence while keeping default Release 1 write authority disabled. The temporary controlled-write smoke document was removed before commit cleanup; the durable smoke evidence remains under the configured FlowDesk state root. Status reloads for both live smoke workflows reported zero stalled lanes.

This helper is diagnostics-only and does not change Release 1 behavior or grant dispatch authority.

On 2026-05-31, the workflow-dispatch model-selection design was updated with a period-normalized usage selection addendum. Raw `remainingPercent` is no longer sufficient as the planned usage ranking basis; the design now uses a period-normalized quota health score (`QHS = remainingFraction - timeRemainingFraction`) over typed usage bucket descriptors, fail-closed handling for stale/unknown/malformed/clock-skewed bucket data, versioned selection policy thresholds, deterministic tie-breakers, redacted selection-rationale evidence, and explicit separation from Provider Health Snapshot diagnostics. The passive TUI/sidebar requirement was also recorded: keep the visible display format unchanged, but choose the representative bucket by lowest period-normalized QHS rather than lowest raw percent.

On 2026-05-31, the first implementation slice for period-normalized usage selection landed in `model-selection-engine.ts`, `workflow-assign-tool.ts`, and `tui-usage-snapshot.ts`. Model selection now carries reset bucket/time/freshness metadata, computes period-normalized quota health, fails closed on stale/unknown/exhausted/malformed bucket data, uses deterministic ranking instead of random weighted selection, and preserves the working-model cache gate. The passive sidebar compact formatter now keeps the same display format but chooses the representative 5h/weekly bucket by lowest period-normalized quota health. Regression coverage was added for period-normalized model selection and unchanged sidebar display format with a changed selected bucket. Focused verification passed with plugin build, model-selection tests, TUI usage snapshot tests, and `git diff --check`.

On 2026-05-31, async agent-task nudge/restart timing was shortened for future lanes: the default quiet period is now 10 seconds, the two automatic nudges occur at approximately 10s and 20s of silence, and async watchdog abort/terminal failure occurs at approximately 30s when both nudges are exhausted. The synchronous capture helper and lane launch timeout were also aligned to the 10s/30s policy where applicable. The project/global FlowDesk main-agent prompt and async-lane conformance notes were updated to use `nudgeQuietPeriodMs: 10000`. Focused verification passed with plugin build, async-lane tests, stall-recovery tests, and `git diff --check`.
