The Gemini coordinator/MCP-vs-active-plugin usage mismatch was root-caused on 2026-05-31. The local OpenCode `google` OAuth record in `auth.json` had an expired access token (expired 2026-05-27), and the collector's expected refresh path uses the refresh token plus the OAuth client id/secret inferred from the locally cached `opencode-gemini-auth@latest` package, which is present. Invoking the installed `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.16` provider-usage tool directly against the same `HOME`/auth/package state successfully refreshes the expired token and returns Gemini `dispatchable`/`ok` (about 65-69% remaining), proving the code, auth discovery, package client inference, and token refresh are all healthy. The coordinator-exposed FlowDesk MCP `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` adapter still returns the stale "gemini oauth client evidence is missing and cached access token is expired" result, so the mismatch is isolated to a stale FlowDesk MCP tool-host process that was not re-launched on the OpenCode restart and is holding a pre-restart plugin/token instance. This is a runtime process-lifecycle issue, not a code defect; restarting the FlowDesk MCP tool host (full coordinator/OpenCode session restart) is the resolution. No code change was required.

A concrete production-dispatch promotion readiness evaluation was run on 2026-05-31 by reloading durable session evidence for `workflow-default-managed-dispatch-20260531` and calling `evaluateFlowDeskProductionEnablementV1`. The reload succeeded but returned zero evidence entries, so the evaluator state is `blocked`, `managed_dispatch_ready=false`, and `dispatch_authority_enabled=false`. The full outstanding blocker set is: `usage_authority_missing`, `runtime_echo_missing`, `telemetry_correlation_missing`, `pre_dispatch_audit_missing`, `production_approval_source_missing`, `dispatch_idempotency_missing`, `provider_health_snapshot_missing`, `configured_verification_missing`, `external_auth_policy_missing`, `sanitized_auth_capture_result_missing`, `provider_policy_missing`, and `lane_conformance_missing`. In other words, none of the required Guard/conformance/provider-health/pre-dispatch-audit/idempotency/approval evidence has been materialized for the promotion workflow yet, so production dispatch promotion stays correctly later-gated and the fallback/reselection and hard-chat gates remain downstream of it. This is the precise remaining work list for any future promotion attempt; no authority was enabled.

A code-review of whether the MCP path should "reload auth every call" confirmed the collector already loads credentials fresh on every invocation: `collectGeminiUsage` re-reads `auth.json` from disk each call, recomputes expiry against `observedAt`, and has no module-level/global credential cache, so the stale MCP result is a tool-host process-lifecycle artifact rather than an in-code auth cache. As an env-drift robustness improvement (not a fix for the stale process), `openCodeGeminiAuthPackageEntrypoints` was hardened to resolve the public `opencode-gemini-auth` OAuth client metadata across all plausible cache homes (configured `OPENCODE_CACHE_DIR`/`XDG_CACHE_HOME` plus the home-relative `~/.cache/opencode` default) and to also try a config-local `~/.config/opencode/node_modules/opencode-gemini-auth` install, so a tool-host launched without those env vars can still infer the client and refresh an expired token. No client secret is stored in FlowDesk source. Regression coverage added two cases (home-cache inference with empty env, and config-local inference) and the full suite passed at 766/766 after `npm run build`.

On 2026-05-31 a live "make it actually run and test it" pass exercised the real dispatch surfaces end to end against the active registry-installed plugin, and recorded both the working path and the fail-closed gates. (1) Tool-registration gating was proven live: loading `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.16` with no injected SDK client registered only the 11 non-dispatch command-backed tools, while loading with an injected SDK client registered 15 tools including `flowdesk_agent_task_run`, `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch`, `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_beta`, and `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_lane_finalize`; lane-launch tools fail closed without a runtime client. (2) A real FlowDesk-owned lane was launched: an in-process OpenCode server (`@opencode-ai/sdk@1.15.10`) plus a real parent session id and `agentRef=agent-reviewer-gpt-frontier` ran `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` with model `openai/gpt-5.5` and prompt `Reply with exactly OK.`, returning `task_completed` with `resultText="OK"` and materializing seven durable evidence records for `workflow-live-lane-echo-20260531c` (`task_result`, two `lane_lifecycle` running+terminal, one `lane_heartbeat`, `agent_task_context`, two `agent_task_progress`). `flowdesk_status_live` then classified the lane `terminal` with zero stalled lanes. Two earlier attempts correctly fail-closed first (`missing_parent_session_binding` with an empty parent session, then `agent_ref must use agent- kind prefix`), and those failed-attempt evidence dirs were cleaned up while the successful `c` workflow evidence was kept as proof. (3) The managed-dispatch promotion gate was exercised live: calling `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_beta` with placeholder approval/audit refs returned `blocked_before_dispatch`, `dispatchAttempted=false`, Guard `reason="Managed-dispatch beta policy mode is required."`, and all authority flags false. (4) The fallback gate was exercised live: `flowdesk_quick_fallback_run` from `openai/gpt-5.5` to `anthropic/claude-opus-4-7` returned `blocked_before_quick_fallback_run` with `automaticFallbackAuthorized=false` and `fallbackAuthority=false`. The hard-chat boundary remains correctly unclaimed: `hasUnsupportedHardChatReturnFields` treats `noReply`/`cancel`/`stop` as unsupported and the chat-hook authority probe pins `noReplySupported=false`/`cancelOrStopSupported=false`. Net result: FlowDesk's real lane-launch path works end to end and produces genuine runtime echo/lifecycle/heartbeat/result evidence, while production managed-dispatch promotion, automatic fallback, and hard chat control all remain fail-closed and later-gated with default Release 1 authority disabled. No synthetic Guard/approval evidence was minted.

On 2026-05-31 a subtask-capture failure was investigated and a diagnostics gap was fixed. While running a real two-lane multi-model design review for a proposed `issueFlowDeskProductionApprovalSourceV1` Guard-approval issuer, the GPT (architecture) lane completed with a substantive `changes_required` review, but the Claude (policy/security) lane returned `task_failed`/`no_response` ("lane launched but no assistant response text found") on two attempts. Root cause was isolated by dumping the raw child-session message stream: the Claude/anthropic prompt failed inside the in-process `@opencode-ai/sdk` server with `UnknownError` so zero assistant messages were produced, whereas the same `anthropic/claude-opus-4-7` model answered fine via the `opencode run` CLI. The difference is the in-process SDK server's anthropic OAuth dispatch path, not the FlowDesk capture code: `observeFlowDeskAgentTaskOutputV1`/`extractAssistantTextFromResponse` correctly reported an empty stream, and the GPT lane proved the capture path works. The capture code therefore needed no change. The diagnostics gap that was fixed: `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` previously collapsed every non-started launch into `sdk_create_failed`. The launch adapter already distinguishes a provider/runtime prompt error (`redactedErrorCategory: "provider_api"`, child session created) from a missing child session, so the runner now maps a `provider_api` launch failure to a new `provider_dispatch_error` task-failure category with a redacted reason explaining the provider rejected the dispatch after session creation. A new `provider_dispatch_error` value was added to `FlowDeskTaskFailedV1.failure_category` and `VALID_TASK_FAILURE_CATEGORIES`, and the redacted reason avoids prompt-like markers so it passes the redaction firewall. Regression coverage in `async-lane.test.ts` asserts a provider-error launch yields `provider_dispatch_error` with durable `task_failed` evidence; the full suite passed 767/767 after `npm run build`. Capture behavior and all dispatch/runtime/authority flags are unchanged. (Separately, the proposed Guard-approval issuer remains design-only and unimplemented; the architecture review's findings — gate-derived required evidence classes, canonical record-digest evidence hashing, action/attempt-bound provider binding, stronger human-confirmation provenance, and issuedAt/TTL/nonce fail-closed checks — are recorded for any future issuer work, and production approval issuance stays a human Guard authority, not code-synthesized.)

Follow-up on 2026-05-31: the suspected "provider OAuth refresh fails on execution" issue was traced to ground truth and found NOT to be a FlowDesk or OAuth defect. The anthropic OAuth access token was valid (about 254 minutes remaining), and the actual server-side error captured from the spawned `opencode serve` log was `Expected a string starting with "ses", got "%7Bid%7D"` — i.e. a URL path placeholder (`{id}`) was not substituted because the ad-hoc diagnosis script called `client.session.prompt`/`messages` in the flat `{ sessionID }` shape instead of the structured `{ path: { id }, body: {} }` shape this SDK build requires. With the structured shape, anthropic answered normally. FlowDesk's production path was already correct: `launchFlowDeskInjectedSdkRuntimeLaneFromPlanV1` uses `callSdkWithLegacyFallback` to try both structured and flat shapes, and re-running the Claude lane through the official `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` path returned `task_completed` with `resultText="OK"`. FlowDesk does not refresh provider tokens itself; it delegates to the OpenCode runtime / auth plugins, which work. No FlowDesk change is required for provider OAuth. The earlier one-off Claude `no_response` was a transient capture-timing/provider hiccup, not a code defect — it reproduced as success. The `provider_dispatch_error` diagnostic granularity added earlier still stands as a genuine improvement for surfacing real future provider-dispatch failures distinctly from generic session-create failures.

Deeper investigation the same day found the Claude lane `no_response` was NOT merely transient: it was a real interaction between slow first-token models and the shortened nudge/timeout policy. Measured first-assistant-token latency on a long review prompt was Claude Opus ~48s vs GPT-5.5 ~4s, while the capture loop's 10s/20s/30s quiet/nudge policy gave up at ~30s with no token, mis-classifying a genuinely-working slow start as `no_response`. The fix adds a heavy-model pre-first-token grace: `isFlowDeskHeavyFirstTokenModelV1` classifies Claude Opus, non-fast GPT-5.x main, and Codex as heavy (explicitly excluding mini/fast/spark/flash/flash-lite/haiku, and per operator decision also excluding gemini pro and sonnet, which keep the unchanged short policy). For heavy models, while no assistant token has appeared yet, the capture loop does NOT nudge (a noReply nudge only interferes with the in-flight first turn) and instead waits quietly with heartbeats until a first-token deadline of `30s * (maxNudges+1) = 90s`, giving up only if no first token arrives in time; once the first token appears, the normal 10s/20s/30s quiet/nudge policy governs the rest of the stream for all models. Regression coverage adds a heavy/light classification test and a heavy-grace slow-first-token capture test (test-only `_heavyFirstTokenGraceMs` override); the full suite passed 769/769. Live reproduction confirmed the fix: the same long-prompt Claude Opus lane that previously failed at ~31s with `no_response` now returns `task_completed` with a real review (and, without the interfering pre-token nudge, completed in ~16s). Capture substance judgement, redaction, and all dispatch/runtime/authority flags are unchanged.

## Release 1 Completion Checklist

Release 1 can be considered complete when the following are true and documented:

1. README, quickstart, user manual, and progress snapshot all reference the current npm version and accurately distinguish default non-dispatch behavior from opt-in provider-calling helpers.
2. A fresh install smoke from npm `0.1.16` passes package-root plugin load in isolated OpenCode 1.15.10 and confirms command-backed tool registration plus chat-intake routing without provider/runtime/lane authority. Bootstrap preview/install and local preview tools have also passed non-interactive smoke. Visual/interactive slash-command display from a real OpenCode TUI session is confirmed for `/flowdesk-doctor`, `/flowdesk-status`, and `/flowdesk-usage`; these remain inert portable command artifacts rather than runtime execution authority.
3. Active profile smoke passes after restart: package-root plugin config loads through `opencode debug config`, `flowdesk_pre_spike_doctor`, provider usage, status follow-up, and TUI plugin loading are verified non-interactively. Quick reviewer subset smoke remains optional/quarantined unless explicitly revalidated.
4. Debug export command path is verified as diagnostic-only with authority false; a recent-workflow file-manifest redaction inspection remains a deeper optional audit check.
5. Any active guarded auto-abort/auto-retry/watchdog options are documented as explicit opt-in diagnostics/recovery, not default Release 1 authority.
6. Final release notes state that hard chat cancellation/no-reply, automatic provider fallback, and production dispatch remain later-gated.

## Overall Assessment

Release 1 foundations are substantially implemented, with default safe local command-backed chat usable without opt-in, Release 1 minimum tools promoted to production-eligible non-dispatch command-backed registration, public npm publication complete for `@flowdesk/core@0.1.0` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.0`, isolated public-registry install/module-load smoke passing, active OpenCode profile registry dependency smoke passing, and user-facing bootstrap docs updated to the public install path. A 2026-05-20 active-environment verification confirmed that the repo build output loads against local OpenCode 1.14.50/plugin dependencies, exposes the Release 1 command-backed tools, and direct doctor/usage/plan/fail-closed-run/approved-fake-runtime-run/status paths work with disabled runtime authority flags. A follow-up patch resolved the chat-routed `/flowdesk-doctor` schema mismatch by making `persist_report` a declared optional boolean in the FDS-1 doctor request schema artifact, with direct handler and chat-routed regression coverage; direct and chat-routed doctor/status/usage/plan-run smoke now pass with runtime authority flags disabled. The repository is published to GitHub at `https://github.com/astasdf1/flowdesk`, the active OpenCode profile now resolves FlowDesk dependencies from the public npm registry while retaining the `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin` plugin entry, and registry publication is no longer the public-distribution blocker for version `0.1.0`. Release 2 now has a core managed-dispatch beta eligibility gate, a separate opt-in adapter boundary that can call the injected OpenCode SDK client only after gate eligibility, explicit opt-in server wiring for guarded actual SDK calls, live OpenAI provider smoke evidence through OpenCode 1.14.50, direct Anthropic Sonnet/Opus diagnostic reachability, non-pure Anthropic SDK success, model catalog metadata inspection, fail-closed audit/gate smoke evidence, live-call audit ordering evidence, schema-valid runtime echo/telemetry evidence, pinned usage-authority evidence validation, all-model auth/usage-missing exclusion diagnostics, an internal provider-native usage collector with unit evidence for Claude OAuth, Codex/OpenAI, and Gemini Code Assist, and redacted live credentialed collector smoke for tested Claude/OpenAI/Gemini usage/quota/reset paths. Release 2/2.5 now also has core production enablement evaluation and approval-decision contracts that combine reloadable durable session evidence, pre-dispatch audit refs, configured verification refs, external auth/provider policy refs, lane conformance refs, explicit approval decisions, blocker labels, and non-blocking uncertainty labels while preserving `dispatch_authority_enabled: false`. Default server behavior remains Release 1 non-dispatch. Remaining production work is wiring these contracts into a production entrypoint, collecting real OpenCode lane observations, and deciding how much incomplete runtime proof to tolerate per opt-in policy. Registered highest-tier reviewer fan-out plus arbitrary agent/model override routing now has a concrete reviewer lane conformance observation artifact for same-model multi-perspective separation, but no default runtime lane launch is enabled.

P8 Background Watchdog (`runFlowDeskWatchdogCycleV1`) was implemented 2026-05-26: opt-in `setInterval`-backed autonomous stall detection and guarded abort/retry cycle, concurrent-execution guard, Guard HMAC re-verify each cycle, per-lane error isolation, optional `flowdesk_watchdog_trigger` MCP tool for Option A external-process fallback, and `.unref()` on the interval so it does not block process exit. 4 new tests added (watchdog cycle abort+retry, guard-invalid skip, concurrent prevention, trigger tool registration). All 573 tests pass.

Generic agent task dispatch tool (`flowdesk_agent_task_run`) was implemented 2026-05-26: added `"agent_task"` to `FLOWDESK_RUNTIME_LANE_LAUNCH_REASONS`, new `FlowDeskTaskResultV1`/`FlowDeskTaskFailedV1` evidence schema in `packages/core/src/task-result.ts` with validators and full property/enum checks, `task_result`/`task_failed` evidence classes added to `state-paths.ts` and `session-evidence.ts`, exported from `core/index.ts`, new `packages/opencode-plugin/src/agent-task-runner.ts` implementing `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` (builds a direct launch plan with `launch_reason: "agent_task"`, launches via injected SDK, extracts assistant text from messages API, writes `task_result.v1` or `task_failed.v1` durable evidence), and new opt-in `flowdesk_agent_task_run` MCP tool registered in `server.ts` behind `agentTaskRun.enabled=true` with `client` and `durableStateRoot` requirements. 15 new tests added (3 core validators + 3 server tool tests). All 588 tests pass.

Generic agent task stall cleanup was patched on 2026-05-27: `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` now writes terminal `lane_lifecycle` evidence for task success and failure paths so completed, launch-failed, and no-response lanes do not remain indefinitely `running` in status/watchdog projections. The patch also adds `flowdesk.agent_task_context.v1` evidence for retry/context recovery with bounded prompt text, prompt hash, concrete agent/model refs, parent session ref, and disabled dispatch authority. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, full `npm test` (592/592), and `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`.

Agent-task recovery backfill was extended on 2026-05-27: added a safe local cleanup helper for legacy generic agent-task lanes that already have `task_failed.v1` or `task_result.v1` evidence while latest `lane_lifecycle` is still `created`/`running`; status reload and the watchdog cycle invoke it before stall projection, writing terminal `no_output` for `no_response` failures, `invocation_failed` for other failures, and `incomplete` with a generic task output ref for successful task-result evidence while preserving all runtime/dispatch authority flags as false. Regression tests cover stale legacy cleanup, `flowdesk.agent_task_context.v1` fallback of agent/model/parent refs, no-response cleanup projecting as terminal with zero stalled lanes, and legacy task-result cleanup without reviewer verdict refs. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, full `npm test` (595/595), and `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`.

Generic agent-task guarded auto-retry was completed on 2026-05-27: P7 retry evaluation now prefers `reviewer_lane_context.v1` but falls back to `flowdesk.agent_task_context.v1` for stalled/aborted generic task lanes, keeping the existing Guard HMAC verification, `autoRetryAfterAbort` opt-in, max retry cap, active pending retry fence, and terminal-aborted lifecycle checks. Generic retries reuse the recorded task id, agent ref, concrete provider-qualified model id, parent session ref, and prompt text from `agent_task_context.v1`, call `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` so new-lane `agent_task_context`, `task_result`/`task_failed`, heartbeat, and terminal lifecycle evidence are written, and record `pending_retry_plan` plus `retry_executed` or `retry_failed` with all authority flags false and no provider/model fallback. `retry_executed.v1` received a minimal safe extension (`retry_kind`, optional `task_id`, optional reviewer-only `perspective`/`original_attempt_id`) so generic task retries can be represented without fabricating a reviewer perspective. Regression tests cover generic retry success, missing generic/reviewer context, cap blocking, and failed generic retry with terminal lifecycle. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, full `npm test` (599/599), and `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`.

Internal subagent taxonomy V2 was drafted and revised on 2026-05-27 in `docs/INTERNAL_SUBAGENT_TAXONOMY_V2.md`: it defines role-specialized internal subagent categories for documentation, exploration, git, backend/frontend/language coding, critical review, architecture, oracle/decision, verification/testing, security/policy, performance, and migration/refactor. FlowDesk review attempts found `changes_required` architecture feedback and incomplete Claude/Gemini reviewer outputs; the doc was revised to state that Release 1 uses the taxonomy only for command-backed planning/status evidence and fake-runtime/degraded lane summaries, while real OpenCode subtask/model/provider launches, write-capable agents, model scoring as production authority, and provider/model reselection remain later-gate work requiring conformance evidence and explicit Guard approval. The doc now also records an OMO comparative-reference boundary, main coordinator allowed/forbidden actions, role-overlap precedence, a role-to-evidence matrix, and a minimum `agent_registry.v1` sketch. No code or OpenCode agent profiles were materialized by this documentation-only update. The reviewer-output failure analysis found likely tool/prompt issues to address before relying on multi-model review as an acceptance gate: quick-reviewer source labels with hyphens fail the validator’s lowercase/underscore source regex, generated reviewer findings missing `required_fix_label` fail typed verdict validation, observation is attempted immediately after lane launch without polling/terminal wait, and generic `flowdesk_agent_task_run` records process-only first assistant messages from reviewer agents as `task_result` without requiring a verdict contract.

Provider usage live cache reuse was patched on 2026-05-27: `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` now attempts a durable snapshot-first lookup from the configured state root and `persistWorkflowId` before invoking provider-native usage collectors, reusing fresh `flowdesk.usage_snapshot.v1` evidence within its `freshness_ttl` for requested provider families. The tool reports `snapshotReuse` with reused evidence ids and skip reasons, still persists newly collected snapshots only when `persistSnapshots=true`, and keeps dispatch/runtime/fallback authority disabled. Regression tests cover fresh snapshot reuse and expired snapshot bypass. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck` and full `npm test` (601/601). Built-dist smoke against `/Users/bagel_macpro_055/.flowdesk` wrote a synthetic fresh Claude usage snapshot and confirmed `snapshotReuse.reusedEvidenceIds` plus `remainingPercent=77`/`alertLevel=ok` without needing a provider-native usage call.

Main-screen FlowDesk lane progress card MVP was added on 2026-05-27: `flowdesk_status_live` now derives bounded `laneProgressCards` from durable lane lifecycle, heartbeat/stall projection, and reviewer verdict refs, and the existing `chat.message` stall/progress surface can opt into `chatMessageStallAlert.includeProgressCards=true` to append a plain-text main chat card for active/recent lanes. The card shows opaque workflow/lane ids, state/classification, last-signal age, agent/model refs, optional verdict label, safe `/flowdesk-status` and `/flowdesk-export-debug` actions, and explicitly says native clickable task UI is not claimed. It does not expose raw prompts, transcripts, provider payloads, or hard chat control fields. The active OpenCode profile was configured with `includeProgressCards=true` and `maxProgressCards=3`; restart is required before that config change takes effect. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, targeted server progress-card tests, and full `npm test` (632/632).

Main-screen progress-card noise was reduced on 2026-05-27: the `chat.message` progress/stall card filter now scopes lane summaries to the current OpenCode chat session's parent-session ref and excludes terminal-only lanes from the plain-text main chat card, while status evidence remains available through `flowdesk_status_live`. This avoids showing completed/incomplete historical lanes or unrelated-session lanes as current “Lane progress.” Regression coverage verifies terminal-only lanes and active lanes from another session do not append `Lane progress:` cards. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck` and the targeted server chat-message stall/progress/auto-abort test filter.

OpenCode TUI sidebar usage display was added on 2026-05-27: `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin` now exposes a separate `./tui` entrypoint that registers a TUI `sidebar_content` slot and displays FlowDesk provider subscription/usage rows for Claude, OpenAI, and Gemini from redacted durable `flowdesk.usage_snapshot.v1` evidence under `workflow-provider-usage-live`. The TUI surface is passive UX only: it reads local durable snapshots, does not call provider APIs or FlowDesk server tools, and carries no dispatch/runtime/fallback authority. The active global OpenCode TUI config was created at `~/.config/opencode/tui.json` pointing at the local built `dist/tui.js` with durable root `/Users/bagel_macpro_055/.flowdesk`; OpenCode restart is required before the sidebar plugin loads. Verification passed with plugin typecheck, targeted TUI usage snapshot tests, plugin build, and full `npm test` (644/644). Node direct import of the TUI module is not a valid smoke in this environment because `@opentui/core` requires the OpenCode/Bun TUI runtime or Node FFI support; runtime conformance should be verified inside OpenCode TUI.

Provider usage sidebar cache regeneration was patched on 2026-05-27: when `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` reuses a fresh durable `flowdesk.usage_snapshot.v1` whose core schema only carries a bucket label such as `claude-5h` rather than a numeric remaining percentage, the tool now preserves the previous fresh redacted sidebar cache percentage for the same `usageSnapshotRef` and recomputes the alert level before rewriting `.flowdesk/ui/provider-usage-sidebar.json`. This prevents a snapshot-reuse run from overwriting useful TUI `%`/alert display with `null`/`unknown` while keeping TUI passive and provider-call-free. Targeted typecheck of the touched provider usage files passed, and a targeted compiled node-test run for `provider-usage-live-tool.test.ts` passed 7/7. The workspace-level plugin typecheck is currently blocked by unrelated pre-existing core test literal-type errors in task authoring/assignment/model-selection tests, so full build/test should be rerun after those unrelated fixtures are corrected.

Gemini OAuth auto-apply for provider usage was patched on 2026-05-27: the core provider usage collector now reads OpenCode's existing `google` OAuth record from `OPENCODE_AUTH_CONTENT` or the local OpenCode auth store (`~/.local/share/opencode/auth.json` / XDG data equivalent) before falling back to `~/.gemini/oauth_creds.json`. This makes FlowDesk usage checks automatically benefit when the user logs into Gemini via `opencode-gemini-auth`, including installs where Gemini was already logged in. For expired access tokens, the collector still honors explicit `FLOWDESK_GEMINI_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID`/`SECRET` or inline config first, then can infer the public OAuth client metadata from the locally cached `opencode-gemini-auth` package so no extra FlowDesk config is needed when the auth package is installed. Regression coverage adds OpenCode-auth valid-token and expired-token refresh cases without storing raw tokens or provider payloads in durable evidence. Targeted provider usage collector tests passed 12/12. Live smoke against the active profile now returns Gemini `dispatchability=dispatchable`, `remainingPercent=96.666664`, `alertLevel=ok`, `resetBucket=gemini-pro-5h`, and persists the Gemini usage snapshot plus sidebar cache. Dispatch/runtime/lane/fallback/hard-chat authority remains unchanged and false.

Compact provider usage sidebar formatting was patched on 2026-05-27: `loadFlowDeskTuiUsageSnapshotViewV1` now preserves per-provider bucket rows from existing `flowdesk.usage_snapshot.v1` evidence (latest per canonical bucket) and from the redacted sidebar cache without changing the usage snapshot schema. The TUI sidebar and provider-usage-enabled `chat.message` main prompt flow render a stable compact three-line format (`Claude`, `OpenAI`, `Gemini`) with 5h and 1w remaining percentages plus absolute ISO-minute reset times, or `✗` for unavailable providers. Provider usage 0%-remaining preservation was patched on 2026-05-28: `packages/core/src/provider-usage-collector.ts` now treats a provider-native `remainingPercent=0`/`remainingFraction=0` result with a reset time as known fresh usage evidence instead of converting it to unknown/insufficient, while still keeping dispatchability and usage-authority acquisition disabled because the provider is exhausted. The core snapshot encodes exhausted known primary buckets as `0% <bucket>` so downstream live usage and passive TUI/sidebar parsing can preserve the numeric value without schema changes; additional bucket snapshots likewise preserve known `0%` buckets as non-dispatchable. Regression coverage in `provider-usage-collector.test.ts` verifies OpenAI/Codex 0% evidence remains fresh, non-dispatchable, has no uncertainty flags, keeps `bucketSnapshot.remainingPercent=0`, and does not mint usage authority. Verification passed with `npm run build && node --test packages/core/dist/provider-usage-collector.test.js` and `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/provider-usage-live-tool.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-usage-snapshot.test.js`. A broad `npm test -- packages/core/src/provider-usage-collector.test.ts` invocation is not a valid targeted command in this repo because it runs the full built suite and then the source test directly, causing a source ESM import failure plus one long-running server test timeout; the focused built tests above passed.

Regression coverage was added for Gemini multi-bucket collection, compact Gemini bucket rendering, and model selection using the three Gemini usage keys separately. TUI usage sidebar cache rendering was patched on 2026-05-27: `packages/opencode-plugin/src/tui.ts` now keeps a shared `FlowDeskTuiUsageSnapshotViewV1` signal in plugin memory and polls `loadFlowDeskTuiUsageSnapshotViewV1` every 30 seconds so `sidebar_content` and optional badges reflect refreshed `.flowdesk/ui/provider-usage-sidebar.json` content without restarting OpenCode and without provider-side calls or schema changes. On 2026-05-29, the first auto-next readiness slice was added so users do not need to repeatedly poll `/flowdesk-status` just to notice that all subtasks finished normally. `flowdesk_status_live` now treats `laneProgressAggregate.autoNextStepEligible=true` as a passive readiness signal and adds `auto_next=ready` to the compact status summary, while task completion paths own the display-only `.flowdesk/ui/auto-next-ready.json` cache listing ready workflows, aggregate counts, task-result refs, and command-backed next action refs. To keep the validation honest, `flowdesk_status_live` no longer materializes or overwrites the TUI Subtask Activity/auto-next cache; it only reports status summaries and durable projections. However, the completion-owned `.flowdesk/ui/auto-next-ready.json` cache remained on the previous workflow timestamp and did not refresh to the new workflow during that smoke, so live TUI cache propagation of the new next-action metadata is not yet proven. Status projection is validated; completion-cache refresh for this new metadata needs follow-up instrumentation or another no-status cache investigation.

Follow-up local hardening on 2026-05-29 added a reconciliation path inside the async child-session monitor: if a monitor pass sees an agent-task child session whose lane already has terminal `task_result` evidence, it still refreshes the display-only completion UI caches before skipping the lane. This covers races where task-result evidence exists but the prior completion-cache write was missed or the process restarted between terminal evidence and UI cache refresh. The patch does not launch, retry, abort, synthesize, call providers, mutate prompts, or grant execution authority; it only re-materializes `.flowdesk/ui/*.json` from existing durable terminal result evidence. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin` and `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js` (24/24), including a regression that a task-result-backed running lifecycle is skipped while the auto-next cache receives `nextActionAvailable=true` and `nextActionKind="synthesis"`. A fresh OpenCode restart is required before live validation of this reconciliation path.

After restart, `workflow-tui-cache-reconcile-post-restart-smoke-20260529` completed with `TUI_CACHE_RECONCILE_OK` and live status again showed `next_action=synthesis_ready`. The UI cache did refresh with next-action metadata, but it was overwritten by an older terminal workflow reconciliation (`workflow-auto-next-trigger-design-20260529`) instead of retaining the newest smoke workflow, exposing a singleton-cache overwrite/order problem. A local follow-up patch now merges completion UI cache entries by workflow/lane rather than replacing the whole cache, sorts ready workflows and sidebar rows by terminal result time, and preserves up to eight display-only ready workflows/rows. This keeps stale terminal reconciliation from erasing newer ready workflows while preserving all authority flags as display-only. Focused verification passed again with plugin build plus `async-lane.test.js`, `status-live-tool.test.js`, and `tui-subtask-activity.test.js` (24/24). Another restart is required to live-validate the merge behavior.

After additional restarts on 2026-05-29, the passive TUI sidebar still held previously rendered `Next ready` and `Subtasks` text even while a fresh live smoke was added and durable status/cache evidence changed. This narrowed the remaining issue from completion-cache writing to TUI reactivity: `sidebar_content` had materialized static text nodes from the initial view. A local patch now makes the TUI lines reactive via memo/accessor-backed text insertion and keeps Subtask Activity polling separate from provider usage polling at 1 second, so updated `.flowdesk/ui/*.json` content should replace the visible sidebar text without another restart after the plugin is loaded. Verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. A fresh OpenCode/TUI restart is required before live-validating the visible sidebar refresh.

Post-restart live validation then proved the durable/status/cache side was healthy for `workflow-tui-reactive-visible-live-smoke-20260529`: `flowdesk_status_live` reported `running/progressing_normal`, and `.flowdesk/ui/subtask-activity-sidebar.json` placed that workflow as the top `running` row. The visible TUI still did not update, and a focused Gemini diagnostic lane found a simple regression in `packages/opencode-plugin/src/tui.ts`: the usage and subtask `setInterval` constants were swapped, so usage was polling every 1s while Subtask Activity/Auto-next only polled every 30s. The local patch restores usage to `USAGE_SIDEBAR_REFRESH_INTERVAL_MS` and subtask/auto-next to `SUBTASK_ACTIVITY_REFRESH_INTERVAL_MS`; verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. Another OpenCode/TUI restart is required to load this corrected polling build before repeating the visible-sidebar smoke.

The sidebar omission diagnosis was refined on 2026-05-29: the visible sidebar was matching the formatter's intentional two-row Auto-next and five-row Subtasks cap, while the Subtask cache retained eight rows and compact labels made distinct workflows appear duplicated as `Live smoke`/`Focused di`. A local patch now aligns the Subtask Activity cache with the visible policy by retaining only the five newest rows and appends a compact task-id suffix to summary-based Subtask labels (for example, `Live smoke #111111`) so duplicate summaries are distinguishable. Auto-next cache limits were left unchanged. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/completion-ui-cache.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. Restart/live validation is still required for the active TUI runtime to load the change.

Subtask Activity ordering was adjusted locally on 2026-05-29 after the visible sidebar showed newer running work below older done/finalizing rows. The root cause was formatter-side priority sorting: cache rows were written by `lastObservedAt`, but `formatFlowDeskTuiSubtaskActivityCompactLines` sorted by state/severity before timestamp, and completed task-result rows often carry `progressPhase="finalizing"`, giving them priority over normal running rows. The formatter now sorts newest `lastObservedAt` first and uses state/severity plus task id only as tie-breakers. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/completion-ui-cache.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. The current display cache remains global to the configured durable state root (`.flowdesk/ui/subtask-activity-sidebar.json`) and is not yet scoped to the current OpenCode chat/session, so recent subtasks from other sessions/workflows can appear until a session-scoped cache/filter is added.

Session-scoped Subtask Activity display support was added locally on 2026-05-29. Completion-owned cache rows now include `parentSessionRef` from `agent_task_context.parent_session_ref`, and the Subtask cache retention cap was raised from five to twenty rows so filtering by the current session has enough recent rows to choose from. The TUI loader accepts an optional `currentParentSessionRef` and filters rows to that session when configured, while preserving global display behavior when no session ref is configured. `tui.ts` now accepts `currentParentSessionRef`/`currentSessionRef` options and passes them into the loader. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/completion-ui-cache.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. Live session scoping still requires the active TUI config/runtime to provide the current parent session ref or an equivalent supported TUI API binding.

The active global OpenCode TUI config (`~/.config/opencode/tui.json`) was updated on 2026-05-29 to pass `currentParentSessionRef="ses-ses_19d3e5cd8fferfe0WE1leJlZYk"` into the FlowDesk TUI plugin, enabling session-filtered Subtask Activity for the current coordinator session after restart. JSON validation passed, and a built-loader preview with that ref returned only rows carrying the same `parentSessionRef`. This is a static config binding for the active session; a future improvement should derive the current session ref from a supported TUI API instead of requiring manual config updates when the session changes.

Follow-up live inspection showed that a newer task from another parent session (`ses-ses_18c004167ffe6pEZCoPi3gC3zf`) was correctly present in durable status but hidden by the static TUI session filter that still pointed at the previous parent session. The active TUI config was updated to the newer parent session ref and validated; a built-loader preview with that ref returned only the matching current-session row (`OpenAI 사용량 #qzt1m8`). This confirms the apparent disappearance was caused by static session-filter configuration, not by state-based ordering. A dynamic current-session binding remains the proper long-term fix.

Auto-next readiness filtering was aligned with Subtask Activity on 2026-05-29. Completion-owned `auto-next-ready.json` workflow rows now carry `parentSessionRef` when all ready rows come from one parent session, the Auto-next TUI loader accepts `currentParentSessionRef`, and `tui.ts` passes the same session filter to both Subtasks and Auto-next. Focused tests now cover Subtask filtering, Auto-next filtering, cache row parent-session materialization, duplicate label suffixes, newest-first ordering, and the twenty-row Subtask cache cap. Verification passed with `npm run build`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/tui-subtask-activity.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/completion-ui-cache.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. Restart is required before the active TUI runtime loads this Auto-next session filter patch.

Managed-dispatch authority gate hardening began on 2026-05-29: `evaluateFlowDeskProductionEnablementV1` now requires at least one reloaded `flowdesk.provider_health_snapshot.v1` evidence record that is fresh, healthy, failure-free, and `dispatchability="dispatchable"` before production enablement can become `dispatch_capable`. Missing, stale, degraded, diagnostic-only, or non-dispatchable provider-health evidence now adds explicit fail-closed blocker labels while keeping default Release 1 dispatch/provider/runtime/lane authority disabled. Regression coverage was added in `production-enablement.test.ts`, and focused verification passed with `npm run build && node --test packages/core/dist/production-enablement.test.js` (18/18). An earlier broad source-test invocation was invalid for this repo shape and timed out after running unrelated tests; the focused built test is the acceptance evidence for this slice.

The managed-dispatch gate was tightened again in the same 2026-05-29 session: production enablement now also requires durable pre-call evidence classes to be reloaded before it can become `dispatch_capable`: `pre_dispatch_audit`, `production_approval_source`, and `dispatch_idempotency`. Missing durable pre-call audit evidence reuses the existing `pre_dispatch_audit_missing` blocker, while missing approval provenance and reservation/replay evidence add `production_approval_source_missing` and `dispatch_idempotency_missing`. `evidenceRefsFromReload` now extracts stable refs from those evidence classes so approval required-ref checks can bind to durable pre-call artifacts. Regression coverage verifies the gate fails closed when those evidence classes are absent. Focused verification passed with `npm run build && node --test packages/core/dist/production-enablement.test.js` (19/19), followed by `git diff --check`.

The same managed-dispatch gate was then made attempt-aware: `FlowDeskProductionEnablementInputV1` can now carry optional `attemptId` and `idempotencyKey`, and when they are present the evaluator requires reloaded pre-dispatch audit evidence to match the workflow, audit ref, target attempt, and approval ref, and requires reloaded dispatch-idempotency evidence to contain a matching `reserved` ledger entry. Drift now fails closed with `pre_dispatch_audit_mismatched` and `dispatch_idempotency_reservation_missing`. Regression coverage was added for target-attempt/idempotency drift. Verification passed with focused build/test (`npm run build && node --test packages/core/dist/production-enablement.test.js`, 20/20), then the full suite (`npm test -- --silent`, 730/730), and `git diff --check`.

Active OpenCode profile configuration was updated on 2026-05-29 to make managed-dispatch reachable after restart for the user's approved dev/beta environment: the FlowDesk plugin options in `~/.config/opencode/opencode.jsonc` now enable `managedDispatchBetaAdapter.enabled=true` and include a bounded `defaultManagedDispatchAuthorization` record (`auth-default-managed-dispatch-20260529`, expiring 2026-05-30T11:30:00Z). This only opens the managed-dispatch registration/route gate; each dispatch call still has to pass the adapter's Guard boundary, durable dispatch manifest, reloaded evidence, consumed approval source, pre-dispatch audit, idempotency reservation, provider/usage/health gates, and exact model match before the SDK prompt call. The authorization record was validated locally with `validateFlowDeskDefaultManagedDispatchAuthorizationV1`; OpenCode must be restarted again for this config change to load.

After restart on 2026-05-29, live doctor confirmed `productionPromotionGate="default_managed_dispatch_authorized_registration_ready"` and `defaultManagedDispatchRegistrationAuthorized=true`. A real managed-dispatch beta smoke was then attempted with the active injected OpenCode SDK client. The first attempt correctly blocked before dispatch on provider-health evidence freshness/source validation. A corrected second attempt (`workflow-managed-dispatch-live-smoke-20260529`, `attempt-managed-dispatch-live-smoke-2`) passed Guard boundary checks, exact model binding, usage evidence, provider-health evidence, runtime compatibility, conformance, telemetry, pre-dispatch audit, durable pre-call evaluation, promotion, and idempotency reservation, then called the injected SDK with `promptAsync`; the adapter returned `status="dispatch_accepted"`, `dispatchAttempted=true`, `realOpenCodeDispatch=true`, `providerCall=true`, `runtimeExecution=true`, `actualLaneLaunch=false`, `fallbackAuthority=false`, and `responseObserved=true`. Status reload for the smoke workflow shows the durable `dispatch_idempotency` reservation evidence (`idempotency-attempt-managed-dispatch-live-smoke-2-reserved`). This proves the managed-dispatch beta route is open and can reach a real OpenCode prompt dispatch under the guarded evidence bundle; result/lifecycle observation remains outside this promptAsync adapter smoke and should be handled by a follow-up managed-dispatch observation slice if needed.

Follow-up hardening on 2026-05-29 closed the promptAsync accepted-but-not-terminalized evidence gap for managed-dispatch beta. `FlowDeskManagedDispatchBetaReservationStoreV1` now has optional `recordDispatchCompleted`, and the durable reservation store materializes a `dispatch_completed` idempotency snapshot after a successful SDK prompt/promptAsync call. If completion-state materialization fails, the adapter reports `dispatch_failed` instead of treating the SDK call as fully accepted without durable completion evidence. Existing failure handling still records `dispatch_failed` on SDK errors. Regression coverage now verifies reserved + completed evidence around successful SDK calls, preservation of previous ledger entries, replay blocking after completion, server-built durable reservation stores, and durable evidence reload. Focused verification passed with `npm run build && node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/managed-dispatch-adapter.test.js` (60/60), then full `npm test -- --silent` passed (730/730), followed by `git diff --check`. A fresh OpenCode restart is required before the active plugin process uses this completion materialization in live managed-dispatch smokes.

Managed-dispatch beta lane-launch mode was then implemented locally on 2026-05-29. `FlowDeskRuntimeLaneLaunchReasonV1` now accepts `managed_dispatch`, and the managed-dispatch request shape supports an explicit `dispatchMode: "lane_launch"`, `allowActualLaneLaunch`, lane/request ids, and a lane title. In lane-launch mode the adapter creates a child session, calls `launchFlowDeskInjectedSdkRuntimeLaneFromPlanV1`, materializes runtime lane lifecycle evidence, and writes the durable `dispatch_completed` idempotency state after successful launch; the redacted server result can include the lane id, child session ref, and message ref. The default prompt mode and Release 1 non-dispatch paths remain unchanged, and the lane-launch path is still gated by the same managed-dispatch boundary, manifest, provider usage/health, approval, pre-dispatch audit, idempotency reservation, exact binding, and explicit `allowActualLaneLaunch=true` checks. Focused adapter verification passed after the change, and a longer-timeout full-suite rerun plus whitespace check passed with `npm test -- --silent && git diff --check` (731/731). A restart is required before the active plugin can exercise `dispatchMode="lane_launch"` in a live smoke.

Provider usage snapshot reuse semantics were adjusted on 2026-05-29 after live managed-dispatch readiness discussion. A fresh dispatchable `provider_usage_snapshot` is now sufficient for the production enablement provider availability gate, so a transient provider-health refresh failure no longer downgrades an otherwise valid recent usage snapshot into `provider_health_snapshot_missing`/`not_dispatchable`. `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` now also treats reused fresh durable usage snapshots as healthy/dispatchable rows for display, preserves a previous fresh sidebar row by provider family when a refresh attempt returns no fresh dispatchable evidence, and avoids persisting failed/non-dispatchable provider-health snapshots over previous usable evidence. Failed refresh attempts are reported as skipped/preserved diagnostics instead of overwriting cached remaining-percent data. Targeted verification passed with `npm run build`, `provider-usage-live-tool.test.js` (8/8), `production-enablement.test.js` (20/20), and `git diff --check`; full verification then passed with `npm test -- --silent && git diff --check` (732/732). A restart is required before the active runtime uses this local patch.

Live runtime inspection after restart showed the first snapshot-reuse patch still missed one OpenAI sidebar shape: the top-level OpenAI row could be a failed refresh (`non_dispatchable`, `remainingPercent=null`) while its `buckets[]` retained a fresh dispatchable weekly or five-hour usage snapshot. The provider-usage live reuse loader now indexes reusable sidebar bucket rows as well as top-level provider rows, ignores bucket reset times already in the past, and can promote a fresh dispatchable bucket to the provider row when the latest refresh fails. This matches the sidebar display semantics users see while still preserving expiry checks and redacted diagnostics. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `provider-usage-live-tool.test.js` (9/9), and `git diff --check`. A restart and live `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` check are required before this bucket-reuse fix affects the active runtime.

Subtask activity sidebar cache refresh was improved locally on 2026-05-29 after a live observation showed `flowdesk_status_live` could see an active `running/progressing_normal` agent-task lane while `.flowdesk/ui/subtask-activity-sidebar.json` still contained only older terminal rows. The root cause is that `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` only refreshed completion/sidebar UI caches after terminal `task_result` persistence; it did not refresh immediately after successful lane launch/heartbeat or after async child-session tracking was written. The runner now calls `refreshFlowDeskCompletionUiCachesV1` after recording the initial running heartbeat and again after async-mode child-session/waiting progress evidence, so the sidebar cache can display a running row during the lane's active window instead of waiting for terminal completion. Regression coverage in `async-lane.test.ts` now asserts `asyncMode` launch writes a `subtask-activity-sidebar.json` row with `state="running"` and `classification="progressing_normal"`. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `async-lane.test.js` (14/14), and `git diff --check`. A restart is required before the active runtime uses this local UI-cache refresh patch.

Follow-up live testing after restart proved the running row was written to `.flowdesk/ui/subtask-activity-sidebar.json`, but the visible TUI sidebar could still lag because `tui.ts` reused the 30-second usage refresh interval for subtask activity. The TUI plugin now keeps provider usage refresh at 30 seconds but polls subtask/auto-next activity every 1 second via a separate `SUBTASK_ACTIVITY_REFRESH_INTERVAL_MS`, so newly launched lanes should appear in the sidebar within about a second after the cache file is written. Focused verification passed with `npm run build`, `tui-subtask-activity.test.js` (7/7), `async-lane.test.js` (14/14), and `git diff --check`. A restart is required before the faster TUI polling is active.

The todo-auto-continuation authority path was scoped on 2026-05-29 after user feedback that remaining todos should be able to progress without silently violating authority boundaries. The implemented first slice is preview-only: new `executeFlowDeskAutoContinuePreviewToolV1` and tool registration `flowdesk_auto_continue_preview` read only durable `workflow_dispatch_plan` evidence plus existing `task_result` task ids to identify the next pending planned task. It returns `nextTaskId`, title/summary, pending/completed counts, and safe command refs while explicitly setting `autoContinuationExecuted=false`, `previewOnly=true`, and all provider/runtime/lane/fallback/hard-chat/tool authority flags false. The tool source of truth is durable FlowDesk plan evidence only; it does not read transient chat/todowrite state, launch a provider lane, execute `/flowdesk-run`, fallback/reselect, mutate TUI/chat, or write workspace files. This gives a safe boundary-respecting stepping stone toward explicit dev/beta continuation: first preview what would continue, then a later gated step can require confirmation/Guard before actual execution. Focused tests cover next-pending-task detection and blocking when no durable plan exists. Verification passed with plugin build plus `auto-continue-preview-tool.test.js`, `status-live-tool.test.js`, `completion-ui-cache.test.js`, `tui-subtask-activity.test.js`, `workflow-synthesis-tool.test.js`, `async-lane.test.js`, and `git diff --check` (33/33). A restart is required before `flowdesk_auto_continue_preview` is available in OpenCode.

Release 1 documentation was refreshed on 2026-05-29 after restart validation and npm-version checks. `npm view` confirmed `@flowdesk/core` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin` latest versions are both `0.1.13`, but an isolated registry install smoke showed that published `0.1.13` does not include the newly implemented `flowdesk_auto_continue_preview` and `flowdesk_workflow_synthesis_preview` tools. The repo packages were therefore bumped to `0.1.14` as the next Release 1 candidate, and README, quickstart, user manual, and package READMEs now point to `0.1.14`. User-facing docs describe provider-free synthesis preview and durable-plan auto-continue preview as local preview helpers with no provider/runtime/lane/fallback/hard-chat/tool authority; they also clarify that `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` remains quarantined by current coordinator policy while explicit `flowdesk_agent_task_run` reviewer lanes are the supported review route. `docs/OPENCODE_CONFORMANCE_PLAN.md` now records these local preview helpers as conformance-safe evidence readers rather than later-gate execution capabilities. A Claude Opus policy/security scan returned `changes_required` mainly for documentation/version/disclosure gaps and quick-reviewer quarantine clarity; the Gemini verification lane ended `invocation_failed`, so it is not counted as acceptance evidence. Publication and isolated npm `0.1.14` smoke are complete for the package-distributed Release 1 preview surface.

Release 1 candidate verification continued on 2026-05-29. The first full `npm test -- --silent` run exposed a real regression in dev-mode workflow dispatch contract handling: process-note output could be reported as completed instead of contract-incomplete. `agent-task-runner.ts` now marks `final_assistant_text` results with `output_kind` `empty`, `process_notes`, or `tool_trace_only` as `missing_contract=true`, and `workflow-dispatch-tool.ts` returns `workflow_dispatch_incomplete` with `redactedBlockReason="output contract not satisfied"` when the terminal task result is contract-incomplete. The regression test now expects a terminal `task_result` with `missing_contract=true` rather than fabricating `task_failed`. Verification passed with full build, targeted workflow-dispatch/status/async tests, full `npm test -- --silent` (727/727), and local tarball install smoke for `@flowdesk/core@0.1.14` plus `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.14`, confirming `flowdesk_auto_continue_preview`, `flowdesk_workflow_synthesis_preview`, status, usage, heartbeat, workflow-dispatch-plan tools, and `chat.message` registration from packed artifacts. After commit `2c53249`, `@flowdesk/core@0.1.14` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.14` were published to npm using token auth without echoing the token; `npm view` verified both latest versions as `0.1.14`. A post-publish isolated registry install smoke in a temporary directory installed both packages from npm and confirmed `flowdesk_auto_continue_preview`, `flowdesk_workflow_synthesis_preview`, status, usage, heartbeat, workflow-dispatch-plan tools, local command tools, and `chat.message` registration.

On 2026-05-28, generic `flowdesk_agent_task_run` parent-session handling was hardened after live failures showed synthetic FlowDesk session refs such as `ses-ses-flowdesk-coordinator` reaching the injected OpenCode SDK and timing out. `packages/opencode-plugin/src/agent-task-runner.ts` now fail-closes before SDK `session.create` when the supplied parent session id is empty, whitespace/unsafe, over-bounded, or already a FlowDesk `ses-...` ref instead of a raw OpenCode parent id, writing redacted `task_failed` plus terminal `invocation_failed` lifecycle evidence with authority flags false and without echoing the raw parent value. `packages/opencode-plugin/src/status-live-tool.ts` now projects generic agent-task lanes that have `task_result` plus legacy `incomplete` lifecycle evidence as `task_result` in lane progress cards so successful generic task output is not presented as an unfinished lane. Regression coverage was added to `server.test.ts` for fail-fast invalid parent refs with zero SDK create/prompt calls and for status card projection of task-result lanes. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test dist/async-lane.test.js`, and focused built server tests for `flowdesk_agent_task_run` (94/94 under the filtered run). `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` remains quarantined by current operator instruction until its normal operation is separately revalidated.

On 2026-05-28, generic `flowdesk_agent_task_run` task display was tightened for operator readability and redaction. Tool responses now include a compact `taskPreview`, explicit `agentName` and `providerQualifiedModelId`, and a multiline `summaryForUser` that shows workflow/lane/task, shortened prompt preview, selected agent, selected model, result or failure reason on separate lines instead of burying the model binding in one sentence. `status_live` lane progress cards now derive bounded prompt previews and task ids from `agent_task_context` plus nudge counts from `agent_task_child_session`; chat.message progress cards render task, prompt preview, agent, model, last-signal age, nudge count, verdict, and issue fields on separate lines. This deliberately exposes only summarized progress metadata, not raw child-session transcripts. The project and active global `flowdesk-main` agent prompts were updated to keep `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` quarantined, prefer `parentSessionId: ""`, and avoid parallel `flowdesk_agent_task_run` launches until concurrent launch stability is revalidated. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `git diff --check`, and focused built server tests for `flowdesk_agent_task_run|progress card` (94/94 under the filtered run). OpenCode restart is required for the active global agent prompt change to take effect.

Post-restart concurrency revalidation on 2026-05-28 kept the parallel `flowdesk_agent_task_run` restriction in place. Two async lanes launched in `workflow-agent-task-concurrency-revalidation-20260528` (OpenAI GPT lane A and Claude Opus lane B) initially produced running lifecycle, heartbeat, child-session, and context evidence, but both reached terminal `invocation_failed` after two nudges and watchdog-abort task failures. The observed result confirms single-lane launches may be used, but concurrent generic agent-task launch remains an active blocker until the SDK/session prompt launch path is stabilized. `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` remains quarantined in both project and active global `flowdesk-main` prompts until explicitly revalidated.

After another OpenCode restart on 2026-05-28, a single-lane `flowdesk_agent_task_run` smoke (`workflow-agent-task-single-smoke-after-restart-20260528`) succeeded with `FLOWDESK_SINGLE_AFTER_RESTART_OK`, confirming the basic post-restart path is usable. Direct investigation found generic agent-task launch was forcing `dispatchMethod: "prompt"` even when the injected SDK exposes `promptAsync`, which can make the launch phase wait on provider completion and contribute to launch timeout/concurrency instability. `packages/opencode-plugin/src/agent-task-runner.ts` now prefers `promptAsync` when available and falls back to `prompt` only when needed; `async-lane.test.ts` adds regression coverage that launch prefers `promptAsync`. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `git diff --check`, and `node --test dist/async-lane.test.js` (6/6). A fresh OpenCode restart is required before live FlowDesk tool smoke can validate the rebuilt plugin path.

Post-restart live validation of the `promptAsync` launch patch on 2026-05-28 confirmed single-lane launch still succeeds (`workflow-agent-task-single-smoke-after-promptasync-restart-20260528`, `FLOWDESK_PROMPTASYNC_SINGLE_OK`) and two concurrent async lanes now both launch immediately with child-session evidence. However, the concurrent async lanes in `workflow-agent-task-concurrency-after-promptasync-restart-20260528` still failed to collect final output and terminalized as `invocation_failed` after two nudges/watchdog aborts. Follow-up code inspection found the async watchdog poller in `stall-recovery.ts` only parsed legacy array/`items` message responses and did not fallback from `sessionID` to current `{ path: { id } }` shape on SDK error, unlike the synchronous agent-task collector. `pollChildSessionText` now handles `data.messages`, `items`, array responses, and SDK-error fallback to the current path shape; watchdog nudges now prefer `promptAsync` before `prompt`. `async-lane.test.ts` adds coverage for current SDK messages response shapes. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `git diff --check`, and `node --test dist/async-lane.test.js` (7/7). Another OpenCode restart is required before live async concurrency can validate this watchdog polling fix.

Post-restart validation of the async watchdog polling fix on 2026-05-28 passed. Single-lane smoke `workflow-agent-task-single-smoke-after-async-monitor-restart-20260528` returned `FLOWDESK_ASYNC_MONITOR_SINGLE_OK`. Two concurrent async generic agent-task lanes in `workflow-agent-task-concurrency-after-monitor-restart-20260528` both launched, were collected by watchdog without nudges (`nudgeCount=0`), wrote `task_result` evidence, and projected as terminal `task_result` cards with zero stalled/progressing-late lanes. Generic agent-task progress evidence was added on 2026-05-28: core now validates and persists `flowdesk.agent_task_progress.v1` under the `agent_task_progress` evidence class with bounded redacted fields (`phase`, `progress_label`, `progress_seq`, `progress_ref`) and hard-false dispatch authority. `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` emits started/waiting/finalizing/failed progress records, and the async watchdog emits nudged/finalizing/failed records while continuing to avoid raw child transcripts and provider payloads. `flowdesk_status_live` lane progress cards and chat progress cards surface the latest redacted progress phase/label alongside prompt preview, nudge count, agent, and model. The project/global `flowdesk-main` prompt wording was reviewed; no further structural rewrite was required beyond bounded fan-out rules already recorded. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `git diff --check`, `node --test packages/core/dist/task-result.test.js` (14/14), `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js` (7/7), and focused built server tests for `flowdesk_agent_task_run executes task|progress card` (94/94 under the filtered run).

A stalled lane analysis on 2026-05-28 found that `workflow-geunteunteun-weekly-compliance-retry-20260528` created a child session and nudge/abort-warning evidence, but its OpenCode child session diff remained `[]`, indicating the prompt was likely never delivered to the child session rather than a provider/model quota issue. The runtime lane launch adapter had been calling `promptAsync` with the flat `{ sessionID, model, agent, parts }` shape first and falling back to `{ path, body }` only on explicit SDK error; in this environment the flat shape can return without error yet not create any child-session message traffic. `launchFlowDeskInjectedSdkRuntimeLaneFromPlanV1` now sends structured `{ path: { id }, body: { model, agent, parts } }` prompt options first for `promptAsync`, falling back to the flat shape only if the SDK reports an error. Regression coverage in `managed-dispatch-adapter.test.ts` verifies structured `promptAsync` is used first for runtime lane launch. Verification passed with plugin build, `git diff --check`, core task-result tests (14/14), async-lane tests (7/7), focused runtime lane launch tests (60/60 under the filtered run), and focused server progress tests (94/94 under the filtered run). Live validation requires restarting OpenCode so the rebuilt plugin code is loaded.

Finalizing-without-terminal lane consistency was patched on 2026-05-28 after live status showed a legacy generic agent-task lane with `agent_task_progress.phase=finalizing` but no `task_result` evidence. Core now validates and reloads `flowdesk.agent_task_inconsistency.v1` under the new `agent_task_inconsistency` evidence class, with deterministic redacted fields, bounded grace-window provenance, safe recovery actions, and `dispatch_authority_enabled=false`. `flowdesk_status_live` now materializes one idempotent inconsistency record when finalizing progress remains without `task_result`/`task_failed` after a durable timestamp grace period, reloads evidence, and projects the lane as `inconsistent_finalizing_without_terminal` rather than terminal/pass/failed. The classification is surfaced separately in status summaries/progress cards with manual recovery actions only; it does not synthesize task results, retry, fallback, provider switch, hard chat control, or any Release 1 authority. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/core && npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/core/dist/task-result.test.js`, `node --test packages/core/dist/lane-stall-projection.test.js`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js`, and `git diff --check`.

Provider Health Snapshot separation was tightened on 2026-05-28: `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` provider rows now expose a bounded `providerHealth` projection separate from usage availability fields, cached usage-snapshot reuse marks health as `unknown`/`diagnostic_only` instead of implying dispatchable health, and opt-in snapshot persistence writes `flowdesk.provider_health_snapshot.v1` under a separate `provider_health_snapshot` durable evidence class alongside usage snapshots. The change keeps usage/quota display separate from health/dispatchability diagnostics and does not grant dispatch/runtime/fallback/hard-chat authority.
