A FlowDesk verification lane was attempted but returned process-only text on the first run, so it was classified as incomplete rather than acceptance evidence; the final-only retry ended as `invocation_failed`, so local focused tests remain the acceptance evidence for this patch.

The async watchdog result-finalization order was hardened on 2026-05-28: `monitorChildSessionsV1` now treats session-evidence writes as success/failure returning operations and writes `agent_task_progress.phase=finalizing` only after `task_result.v1` persistence succeeds. If task-result persistence fails, the watchdog records a redacted `task_failed.v1` and failed progress label instead of creating progress-only finalization, preserving the existing no-raw-transcript/no-authority behavior. Regression coverage in `async-lane.test.ts` forces the task-result write-failure branch and asserts no `task_result` or finalizing progress is written while a redacted failure record is produced. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js` (8/8), and `git diff --check`.

Generic agent-task result persistence was patched on 2026-05-28 after durable failure evidence showed repeated `watchdog could not persist task_result evidence` records. The common path was watchdog-collected or synchronous assistant text containing redaction-forbidden markers such as prompt/raw-log/path wording, causing `flowdesk.task_result.v1` validation to reject otherwise useful output. The core `task_result` validator now treats `result_text` as bounded final-output evidence rather than metadata for raw-marker key/value scanning, while still validating all metadata and authority fields fail-closed. `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` and `monitorChildSessionsV1` preserve marker-like final output text up to the existing 32KB cap, hash the original collected text, and check evidence-write success before recording finalizing progress. Downstream reuse remains bounded: status/progress cards do not expose full `result_text`, export-debug remains redacted-section based, and workflow synthesis still clamps or redacts task-result snippets before feeding them to a synthesis lane. Regression tests cover watchdog and synchronous preservation of marker/path-containing output, core acceptance of bounded final output text with marker-like wording, and successful `task_result` persistence instead of `task_failed`. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js` (10/10), `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/core`, `node --test packages/core/dist/task-result.test.js packages/core/dist/state-foundation.test.js packages/core/dist/index.test.js` (56/56), and `git diff --check`. Earlier post-restart simple and marker-heavy live smokes succeeded with `task_result`/terminal status before the final no-masking refinement; another restart is required before live smoke reflects the no-masking build.

Usage-aware reviewer routing guidance was added on 2026-05-28 to the project and active global `flowdesk-main` agent prompts. Multi-perspective review fan-out must now call `flowdesk_provider_usage_live` first and avoid blindly using every top model when a provider row is `critical`, `exhausted`, `stale`, `unknown`, or `non_dispatchable`. The documented binding policy keeps Claude Opus, GPT frontier, and Gemini Pro as preferred healthy defaults, but routes Gemini Pro critical/exhausted cases to Gemini Flash Lite first (`google/gemini-3.1-flash-lite-preview`) and then OpenAI GPT if Flash Lite is unavailable; similarly, Claude/OpenAI critical cases can move the affected perspective to another healthy provider while preserving the perspective label in the task prompt. This was corrected from the earlier `google/gemini-3.1-flash-preview` wording after EDC reviewer evidence showed OpenCode reporting that model id as unavailable and suggesting Flash Lite/Image variants. The prompt explicitly states this is pre-launch usage-aware reviewer binding, not managed fallback/reselection authority. A design lane was attempted but returned process-only text, so the prompt update itself and usage-live evidence are the acceptance basis. OpenCode restart is required for the active global agent prompt change to take effect.

EDC live-environment reviewer failure remediation was recorded on 2026-05-28. Repeated Claude Opus review failures in the EDC OpenCode project were traced to read permission prompts for env-style files rather than Claude quota/provider failure; the active profile and EDC local config were changed to `read: allow`, and `workflow-edc-read-allow-smoke-20260528` verified `EDC_READ_ALLOW_SMOKE_OK` with `nudgeCount=0`, no stalled/progressing-late lanes, and log evidence showing `permission=read ... action=allow`. The Gemini reviewer fallback model id was also corrected from unavailable `google/gemini-3.1-flash-preview` to `google/gemini-3.1-flash-lite-preview`, with live smoke evidence returning `EDC_GEMINI_FLASH_LITE_OK`; Gemini Pro quota remains critical, so usage-aware routing should continue to avoid Gemini Pro for large review work until reset.

Terminal-aware generic agent-task result collection was started on 2026-05-28 after live evidence showed OpenAI reasoning/process parts being persisted as `task_result` before the child session's final assistant text and `reason:"stop"` step-finish were observed. A new shared plugin helper (`agent-task-output.ts`) now ignores reasoning parts, tracks latest assistant text candidates, detects terminal step-finish markers, classifies output kind, and records optional task-result quality metadata (`completion_status`, `output_kind`, `usable_for_synthesis`, `missing_contract`) while preserving backward compatibility for older `task_result.v1` records. The watchdog no longer finalizes on the first assistant text without a terminal marker, captures terminal final text as final output, and can preserve useful candidate text as partial output at abort time instead of losing all information; the synchronous collector follows the same terminal-aware observation model. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/core`, `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, and `node --test packages/core/dist/task-result.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js` (31/31). Event-hook based terminal observation remains a later hardening step after polling semantics are stabilized in live smoke.

Status/watchdog regression coverage was broadened on 2026-05-28: `status-live-tool.test.ts` now covers finalizing progress paired with valid `task_result.v1` and `task_failed.v1` evidence and asserts `flowdesk_status_live` does not materialize `agent_task_inconsistency` for terminal-backed finalizing states. Together with the existing idempotent inconsistency test and watchdog write-failure guard test, this pins the desired distinction between unmatched finalizing progress and terminal-backed finalization. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/async-lane.test.js` (13/13), and `git diff --check`.

Status live now surfaces terminal-aware task-result quality metadata on lane progress cards (2026-05-28). `flowdesk_status_live` carries optional `completionStatus`, `outputKind`, and `usableForSynthesis` fields from `task_result.v1` into each bounded `laneProgressCards` entry, so partial/process-note outputs can be distinguished from final answers without exposing full result text. A live partial smoke (`workflow-terminal-aware-live-smoke-20260528-partial`, lane `lane-task-mppiosaf`) produced terminal `task_result` evidence with `completion_status="final"`, `output_kind="process_notes"`, and `usable_for_synthesis=true`, confirming the metadata path works against real OpenAI output. Regression coverage asserts the fields are projected for task-result-backed finalizing states. Verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js`, and `git diff --check`.

Subtask UI improvement work started on 2026-05-28 after committing terminal-aware collection. The chat.message lane progress card renderer now carries the status-live task-result quality fields through its bounded lane-card summary and prints a compact `result: <completion>/<kind>/synthesis=<bool>` line, defaulting to `result: (none)` for active lanes without task-result evidence. This keeps full `result_text` hidden while making partial/process-note/final-answer state visible when result metadata is present. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test --test-name-pattern "progress card" packages/opencode-plugin/dist/server.test.js`, and `git diff --check`. A scout lane for additional UI opportunities (`workflow-subtask-ui-improvement-scout-20260528`) returned process-only text, so it is treated as incomplete and not used as acceptance evidence.

Permission-awaiting subtask design was drafted on 2026-05-28 as a next UI/orchestration target. The desired behavior is: when a FlowDesk generic agent-task child session reaches an OpenCode permission request, FlowDesk should surface a main-session status/permission card and suspend watchdog nudge/abort/no-response timeout while that permission remains unresolved. The design must not auto-approve permissions or claim native UI control without OpenCode conformance evidence. Required shape: a redacted `flowdesk.agent_task_permission_wait.v1` evidence record (`awaiting_user`/`resolved`/`denied`/`expired`), an `awaiting_permission` progress phase or equivalent projection, status/chat cards that show the bounded requested action label, manual `/flowdesk-abort` still available, and watchdog logic that treats unresolved permission wait as `awaiting_dependency` rather than stalled. Critical gate: before implementation, verify against actual OpenCode SDK/docs/code that child-session permission requests are observable, identify the event/message shape, and prove whether the native permission UI can be surfaced or whether FlowDesk can only display a diagnostic card. Four attempted reviewer lanes for this design completed terminally but returned process-only planning text, so they are classified incomplete and not acceptance evidence; this reinforces the need for task-result quality metadata and automatic all-lanes-terminal synthesis/notification before relying on reviewer lanes for design signoff.

Event-hook based subtask orchestration design was updated on 2026-05-28 after confirming OpenCode 1.15.6 exposes both plugin `Hooks.event(input: { event })` and SDK `client.event.subscribe` SSE `/event`. The event model should be the primary lane-progress path, with status polling/watchdog scans retained only for recovery, replay, and missed-event fallback. The design maps FlowDesk child-session events to lanes through durable `agent_task_child_session` binding, treats `message.part.updated` step-finish and `session.idle` as terminal-check candidates, `session.error` as a terminal-failure candidate, `session.status: retry` as non-terminal retrying, tool-part `state:error` as a non-terminal tool issue unless followed by session-level terminal/error evidence, `permission.updated/replied` as permission-wait lifecycle input, and `session.updated` only as metadata refresh/heartbeat/terminal-check trigger rather than direct completion. A workflow wait-set/aggregate card should track expected/running/completed/failed/awaiting-permission counts with event-id/digest idempotency, attempt isolation, replay protection, and stable card ids. When every expected lane in the current attempt completes normally with usable final task results and no unresolved permission wait, no task_failed, no finalizing inconsistency, and no contract-missing result, FlowDesk should automatically advance to the next planned orchestration step without requiring the user to ask for status: for review/analysis fan-out this means starting the synthesis/summary step immediately; for execution-like or write-capable next steps it may only prepare the next-step card and require the existing Guard/confirmation boundary. If any lane fails, is partial, is awaiting permission, or has contract/inconsistency evidence, automatic continuation must stop and surface retry/abort/resume/summarize-partial choices instead. This automatic normal-completion continuation is a required UX goal because the current manual `/flowdesk-status` polling loop forces the user to ask whether subtasks ended before the coordinator can proceed.

The first event-hook implementation slice landed locally on 2026-05-28. `server.ts` now registers an OpenCode plugin `event` hook whenever a durable state root is configured, even when natural-language routing is disabled. The hook routes OpenCode events through a new `event-hook-observer.ts` module, maps event `sessionID` values to FlowDesk lanes using durable `agent_task_child_session` evidence, records bounded `agent_task_progress.v1` updates for `permission.updated`, `permission.replied`, `session.status`, `session.idle`, `session.updated`, `session.diff`, and `message.part.updated`, and materializes `task_failed.v1` plus terminal `lane_lifecycle state=invocation_failed` for mapped `session.error` events. Core progress phases now include `awaiting_permission` and `retrying` so permission waits and OpenCode retry status can be represented without overloading generic waiting. Focused synthetic hook tests cover permission progress and session-error terminal failure. This is Phase 1 observation/materialization only: wait-set counts, all-lanes-normal automatic synthesis/continuation, real live OpenCode event smoke, and watchdog permission-suspend behavior remain next slices.

The same local slice also fixes the status projection regression exposed by event-hook design smokes: lanes with valid `task_result.v1` or `task_failed.v1` evidence may still have older `agent_task_inconsistency.v1` records from previous status checks, but status projection must not continue classifying them as `inconsistent_finalizing_without_terminal`. `flowdesk_status_live` now prunes stale inconsistency snapshots from the projection input when terminal task evidence exists for the lane, while preserving the historical evidence count. Regression coverage seeds a legacy inconsistency plus task_result and asserts the progress card projects as `terminal`. Focused verification passed with core/plugin builds, `task-result.test.js`, `status-live-tool.test.js`, targeted server `event hook|progress card` tests, and `git diff --check`.

After OpenCode restart on 2026-05-28, the event hook path was live-smoked with `workflow-event-hook-live-restart-smoke-20260528`: the lane produced many `agent_task_progress` records with labels such as `agent task message.updated event observed`, proving the active plugin receives OpenCode `Hooks.event` callbacks for child-session events. The lane then completed with `EVENT_HOOK_RESTART_SMOKE_OK`, `task_result`, terminal projection, and zero stalled/progressing-late/inconsistent lanes. Phase 2/3 local work also added `laneProgressAggregate` to `flowdesk_status_live` summaries (`expected`, `terminal`, `taskResult`, `failed`, `awaitingPermission`, `normalCompleted`, `autoNextStepEligible`) and chat progress cards now render aggregate task counts when available. `monitorChildSessionsV1` now suspends polling nudge/abort for lanes whose latest/event progress indicates `awaiting_permission`, resuming only after a permission-response progress marker. Focused regression coverage verifies permission-wait watchdog suspension, event-hook permission progress, event-hook session-error terminal failure, aggregate auto-next eligibility for normal terminal task results, status inconsistency pruning, and progress-card rendering.

Developer-only OpenCode UI conformance probing was added locally on 2026-05-28 after user testing showed that task start/completion evidence is durable but not easy to inspect from the UI. `server.ts` now registers a guarded `flowdesk_ui_probe` tool only when `FLOWDESK_UI_PROBE=1` or plugin option `uiProbe.enabled=true`; it emits bounded markdown `<details>`, link, code-fence, and long-log samples and reports redacted recent OpenCode event observations captured by the plugin `event` hook. The probe also records event summaries when no durable state root is configured, but does not grant dispatch, provider-call, runtime, fallback, write, hard-cancel/noReply, or custom UI authority. This is intentionally temporary conformance instrumentation to determine whether OpenCode supports clickable links, collapsible markdown/details, tool-output folding, click/key event propagation, or message update/replace behavior in the real TUI. Verification so far: `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, targeted server `event hook|progress card` tests, and `git diff --check` passed. Active global OpenCode plugin options now set `uiProbe.enabled=true`, so OpenCode restart is required before live UI observation; remove that option or unset the env flag/revert the small probe registration after conformance evidence is collected.

Live UI probe and reviewer follow-up on 2026-05-29 clarified the practical Release 1 task-progress UI direction. In the active OpenCode UI, tool calls appear as a compact one-line invocation, tool result bodies are not reliably visible as expanded cards/logs, markdown `<details>` renders as plain text rather than a collapsible widget, and the event buffer showed `session.*`, `message.*`, and `todo.updated` activity but no click/key interaction events. The first deep-research lane (`workflow-ui-alternatives-deep-research-20260529`) ended `invocation_failed`, so it is not acceptance evidence; the narrowed retry (`workflow-ui-alternatives-deep-research-retry-20260529`) completed with usable `task_result` and recommended high-confidence plain assistant summaries plus command-backed `/flowdesk-status`/`/flowdesk-doctor`/`/flowdesk-export-debug` as the primary Release 1 surfaces, with todo/status-style events only medium-confidence/conformance-gated. A separate architecture review lane (`workflow-ui-alternatives-practical-plan-20260529`) returned `changes_required`: assistant-visible auto summaries need a redaction-first bounded allowlist, `chat.message` additions must remain additive steering-only without replacing/suppressing the original turn, execution-like commands still require visible confirmation, sidebar/status and click/key/control surfaces remain conformance-gated, debug log artifacts must stay under `.flowdesk/` with write-time redaction, OSC 8 hyperlinks need plain-text fallbacks, and Release 1 should prioritize at most two low-risk surfaces. The resulting plan is to use compact redacted assistant-visible summaries and durable command-backed status/debug/export surfaces for Release 1, while deferring clickable/collapsible/sidebar/native-control UX until OpenCode conformance evidence proves a supported API. `flowdesk_ui_probe` should remain treated as temporary guarded instrumentation and be disabled or removed after the conformance evidence is recorded.

The persistent background-task UI idea was split into a later-gate R2-R5 track on 2026-05-29 rather than rejected as a Release 1 constraint violation. The accepted direction is: keep R1 conservative with compact assistant-visible summaries plus command-backed status/debug/export, then pursue an experimental display-only task indicator/dock/status-strip track for later gates. Proposed gate matrix: R2 discovers official OpenCode TUI/footer/sidebar/status-slot APIs and, only if present, prototypes a read-only task indicator; R3 explores a local companion/webview that reads redacted durable evidence only; R4 enriches the dock with heartbeat-synchronized lane state and recovery affordance labels that still route through existing commands; R5 targets an upstream/first-class always-visible footer/status strip if OpenCode exposes one. The display-only authority contract is explicit: persistent UI surfaces may show durable lane/task/heartbeat evidence but must not approve dispatch, cancel sessions, issue `noReply`, perform fallback/reselection, write files, mutate prompts, or replace/suppress chat turns. OMO-like patterns are acceptable only as visible, non-mutating UX patterns; hidden prompt/prefix injection remains disallowed. The minimal first patch for this track should avoid rendering a new persistent UI and instead add/discover host UI capabilities, factor a reusable redacted lane snapshot helper for future surfaces, and document falsifiable conformance acceptance criteria such as state fidelity to durable evidence, read-only authority rejection, no chat-history mutation, redaction safety, graceful degradation when the API is absent, and OpenCode-version-bound evidence.

The later-gate UI track was refined on 2026-05-29 to explicitly include a **Subtask Activity Panel/Dock** for checking subtask activity and redacted logs/details. This is now a first-class goal rather than an implied part of the persistent UI work. The panel should list FlowDesk-owned lanes/subtasks across running, completed, failed, blocked, permission-waiting, retried, and recently completed states, showing bounded fields such as workflow/lane/task ids, task preview, agent/model label, lifecycle/stall classification, latest progress label, heartbeat/nudge counts, task-result quality, reviewer verdict summary, safe evidence refs, and command-backed safe next actions. Click/expand behavior is allowed only when an official OpenCode UI surface supports interaction; expanded views must show redacted lifecycle/progress/verdict/result-quality timelines and links or commands for `/flowdesk-status`, `/flowdesk-export-debug`, `/flowdesk-retry`, `/flowdesk-resume`, and `/flowdesk-abort`, not raw provider transcripts or prompts. If official UI interaction is unavailable, the R2 surface should degrade to a read-only sidebar/footer count plus top active rows, with details available through status/export commands; richer filtering, grouping, timeline, and log inspection can move to the R3 companion/webview or R4 dock. The minimal first patch should add a normalized `subtaskActivityRows`/lane snapshot projection from durable evidence and only then wire the earliest available read-only UI surface.

The first minimal Subtask Activity Panel foundation patch was implemented locally on 2026-05-29. `flowdesk_status_live` now includes a bounded `subtaskActivityRows` projection per workflow, derived from existing redacted lane progress cards and carrying workflow/lane/task ids, state, stall classification, latest progress phase/label timestamp, nudge count, task-result quality fields, verdict label, failure hint, and safe `/flowdesk-status`/`/flowdesk-export-debug` refs. The projection intentionally does not render a persistent UI yet and does not expose raw prompts, transcripts, provider payloads, credentials, dispatch/cancel/noReply/fallback/write authority, or hidden mutation. Task ids can now be projected from task-result evidence when an agent-task context record is absent. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js`, and `git diff --check`.

Network-interruption recovery hardening was patched locally on 2026-05-29 after live work showed lanes can appear to stop or generate duplicate terminal evidence around connectivity/plugin interruptions. The immediate observed lane (`workflow-subtask-activity-ui-connection-plan-20260529`) had actually completed with `task_result`, but follow-up recovery investigation lanes demonstrated the same failure mode family: a provider lane can continue emitting progress, become progressing-late, then terminate as `invocation_failed` or partial output after nudges/watchdog handling. The patch adds a core `network_interrupted` task-failure category for stale post-restart/no-response cases, adds a just-in-time terminal task-evidence check in `monitorChildSessionsV1` before writing watchdog task results or failures to reduce duplicate `task_result`/terminal evidence when multiple watchdog/status passes race after reconnect, and extends `subtaskActivityRows` with `recoveryActionRefs` so failed/late/stalled rows can advertise `/flowdesk-retry`, `/flowdesk-resume`, `/flowdesk-abort`, and export/status commands while normal rows show status/export only. This is still metadata/recovery affordance hardening, not automatic provider fallback, hard cancel/noReply authority, or UI-side execution authority. Focused verification passed with core/plugin builds, `task-result.test.js`, `async-lane.test.js`, `status-live-tool.test.js`, and `git diff --check`.

After OpenCode restart on 2026-05-29, live status confirmed the rebuilt network-recovery and subtask-activity metadata were loaded: `subtaskActivityRows` included `recoveryActionRefs`, and a new post-restart smoke (`workflow-network-recovery-post-restart-smoke-20260529`) completed with `NETWORK_RECOVERY_POST_RESTART_OK`, terminal `task_result`, and zero stalled/progressing-late/inconsistent lanes. A low-risk user-visible UI connection was then added locally: `flowdesk_status_live.summaryForUser` now includes a compact `subtasks=` preview per workflow, capped to three rows, showing lane id, state, stall classification, and compact recovery action labels such as `status|retry|resume|abort|export-debug`. This makes Subtask Activity Panel data visible immediately through the existing status surface while sidebar/click/expand UI remains later-gated. Focused verification passed with `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/status-live-tool.test.js`, and `git diff --check`.

GPT reviewer `tool_calls_only_no_verdict` root cause fixed on 2026-05-27: `messageTextCandidates` in `managed-dispatch-adapter.ts` previously only captured message-part text that was exactly `{...}` (starts with `{`, ends with `}`). GPT frequently wraps the JSON verdict in markdown code fences (``` ```json ... ``` ```) or adds preamble prose before the JSON object, both of which caused the text to be silently dropped, producing `tool_calls_only_no_verdict` or `missing_verdict` terminal states on otherwise-correct responses. The new `extractJsonBlocksFromText` helper first checks for a bare `{...}` object, then extracts JSON from code fences via regex, and finally falls back to scanning for the last balanced `{...}` block in the text. Two new regression tests cover the code-fence case and the preamble-with-JSON case. Workspace typecheck + full `npm test` passed: 662/662. Live verification via `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` post-restart returned `workflow-quick-reviewer-mpnmtmk2` with all 3 lanes `verdict_observed`/`complete` and `verdicts=pass/pass/pass`, confirming no more `tool_calls_only_no_verdict` for GPT. Dispatch/runtime/lane/fallback authority unchanged and false.

FlowDesk doctor `geminiOAuthConfigured` field extended on 2026-05-27: the field previously only reported `true` for explicit inline `geminiOAuthClientId/Secret` config or `FLOWDESK_GEMINI_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID/SECRET` env vars. It now also returns `true` when the OpenCode auth store (`~/.local/share/opencode/auth.json` / XDG data path) contains a valid `google` or `gemini` OAuth record (type=oauth with access or refresh token), matching the auto-detect credential path that was added for the collector. A new private `geminiOAuthAutoDetectAvailable` helper reads the auth store fail-closed; no raw tokens are logged or echoed. Full `npm test` passed: 668/668. No dispatch/runtime/lane/fallback authority change.

FlowDesk-owned lane enforcement was made explicit on 2026-05-27 after a non-FlowDesk raw subtask path was identified as bypassing durable lane monitoring. The project `AGENTS.md`, project `.opencode/agent/flowdesk-main.md`, and active global `~/.config/opencode/agent/flowdesk-main.md` now state that any delegated FlowDesk subtask must use only FlowDesk-owned tools (`flowdesk_agent_task_run`, `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run`, `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch_plan`, or explicitly gated FlowDesk dispatch tools) that emit durable lane lifecycle/status/heartbeat evidence. Raw OpenCode `task`, background task sessions, ad-hoc subagents, nested `opencode run`, OMO/OMC/Sisyphus, and any non-FlowDesk-owned lane are forbidden for FlowDesk planning, implementation, review, verification, or investigation even when no FlowDesk lane is available; the coordinator must stop/report the blocker or perform bounded direct main-session patch/edit work instead. The active global FlowDesk main agent permission now sets `task: deny`; OpenCode restart is required for the global agent change to take effect.

Quick reviewer result collection was patched on 2026-05-27 after stalled reviewer lanes were observed: `executeFlowDeskRuntimeReviewerExecutionBridgeV1` now waits on injected SDK `session.messages` before verdict observation using explicit terminal/message signals or bounded stable final-output detection, reuses the observed message snapshot for verdict parsing, and writes terminal `timeout`, `invocation_failed`, `missing_verdict`, or `tool_calls_only_no_verdict` lane lifecycle evidence for incomplete paths so status projections do not leave those lanes indefinitely running. Quick reviewer source labels are normalized to the verdict validator's lowercase/underscore contract, the reviewer prompt now requires `required_fix_label` on kept findings and avoids placeholder wording, verdict candidate selection prefers later/final assistant JSON while capping validation errors, and `flowdesk_agent_task_run` now prefers final assistant text with an explicit internal output-contract guard for process-only responses. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/quick-reviewer-run.test.js packages/opencode-plugin/dist/server.test.js`, and `node --test packages/opencode-plugin/dist/managed-dispatch-adapter.test.js`.

Internal subagent taxonomy and `agent_registry.v1` core contracts were advanced on 2026-05-27: `docs/INTERNAL_SUBAGENT_TAXONOMY_V2.md` now orders recommended implementation around registry/output contracts/planning validation/status acceptance before materializing agent files, states that multi-perspective reviewer lanes count as acceptance evidence only after completion-wait, typed verdict validation, durable `reviewer_verdict`, complete terminal lifecycle, and terminal/complete status reload all succeed, and records that stale/restarted workflow cleanup via evidence-only abort/backfill is recovery evidence rather than approval. `packages/core/src/agent-registry.ts` adds standalone `flowdesk.agent_registry_entry.v1` and `flowdesk.agent_registry.v1` validators that reject unknown properties, invalid agent ids/release gates, forbidden raw payload markers, authority-smuggling language, missing mandatory forbidden-action boundaries, `fallback_allowed: true`, and `dispatch_authority_enabled: true`; exports were added from `packages/core/src/index.ts`. New `packages/core/src/agent-registry.test.ts` coverage passed alongside targeted core typecheck/build.

Agent registry output-contract and role/evidence compatibility validation was added on 2026-05-27: `packages/core/src/agent-registry.ts` now exports allowed role categories (`documentation`, `exploration`, `git`, `implementation`, `review`, `architecture`, `decision`, `verification`, `security`, `performance`, `migration`), redaction-safe output contract refs (`contract-task-result-v1`, `contract-reviewer-verdict-v1`, `contract-verification-result-v1`, `contract-policy-review-result-v1`, `contract-architecture-decision-result-v1`, `contract-migration-plan-result-v1`), and allowed registry evidence classes including current session/lifecycle classes plus typed placeholder classes. Entry validation now rejects invalid role/output/evidence values, advisory review entries that require `reviewer_verdict`, verification entries missing `lane_lifecycle` or task/verification evidence, implementation entries outside `release1_planning_only`/`later_gate_scoped_write`, security output/permission refs that imply Guard or dispatch approval, entries lacking terminal-equivalent evidence, `dispatch_authority_enabled: true`, `fallback_allowed: true`, and authority-smuggling refs/strings. `docs/INTERNAL_SUBAGENT_TAXONOMY_V2.md` names these contract refs and clarifies that typed verification/policy/architecture/migration contracts are placeholders until concrete durable evidence schemas exist. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck --workspace @flowdesk/core`, `node --test packages/core/dist/agent-registry.test.js`, and full `npm test` (619/619). No real dispatch, fallback, OpenCode agent file materialization, or session evidence wiring was added.

Workflow-dispatch planning contract was added on 2026-05-27: `packages/core/src/workflow-dispatch-plan.ts` defines `flowdesk.workflow_dispatch_plan.v1`, selected `agent_role`/`agent_role_ref` hints, task graph records, diagnostic-only model-selection refs/labels, and hard false Release 1 authority flags (`dispatch_authority_enabled`, `provider_call_made`, `runtime_execution`, `actual_lane_launch`). Validation rejects unknown properties, authority-smuggling language, provider/model fallback or reselection wording, true authority flags, invalid role categories, registry-mismatched role refs when an `agent_registry.v1` is supplied, runtime launch refs, and raw payload markers. The pure evaluator returns only an inert planning artifact and false runtime flags; exports and schema-registry metadata were added. `docs/INTERNAL_SUBAGENT_TAXONOMY_V2.md` now marks registry/output contract work and the core workflow-dispatch planning contract as complete while deferring `/flowdesk-plan` public `agentRole`, server/local-adapter `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch`, fake-runtime/degraded lane evidence emission, `summaryForUser` aggregation, and durable planning/status wiring. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck --workspace @flowdesk/core`, targeted `node --test packages/core/dist/workflow-dispatch-plan.test.js packages/core/dist/agent-registry.test.js packages/core/dist/plan.test.js`, and full `npm test` (624/624).

Workflow-dispatch planning evidence was wired into durable session evidence/status on 2026-05-27: `workflow_dispatch_plan` is now a managed session evidence class under `.flowdesk/sessions/<workflow>/evidence/workflow-dispatch-plan`, reload validation uses the Release 1-safe `flowdesk.workflow_dispatch_plan.v1` validator, and live status summaries report the latest plan revision/task count while keeping real dispatch, provider calls, runtime execution, lane launch, fallback, and hard chat authority false. Public Release 1 command registration remains unchanged to avoid disturbing the FDS-1 minimum command surface; future local-adapter or `/flowdesk-plan` role-hint integration should stay opt-in/internal-only unless the minimum command contract is deliberately updated.

On 2026-05-31, managed-dispatch beta was tied more tightly to the durable working-model cache. `dispatchManagedDispatchBetaPromptV1` now checks `~/.flowdesk/model-availability/working-models.json` (via the configured durable root) before SDK dispatch and blocks redacted managed dispatch when the guard-approved provider-qualified model is absent or the cache is missing/unreadable. The new regression coverage keeps the existing root-optional behavior, proves cache-backed allow/deny behavior, and updates the server-state-root tests to create working-model evidence before launch. Focused build and managed-dispatch tests pass; a full `npm test` run still surfaced two unrelated pre-existing `status-live-tool.test.js` cache assertions.

Later on 2026-05-31, those `status-live-tool.test.js` cache assertions were resolved by making `flowdesk_status_live` call the terminal backfill path without refreshing completion UI caches, so status reads remain read-only while completion-owned paths continue to own `.flowdesk/ui/*` updates. Full `npm test` now passes again.

On 2026-05-31, the subtask result pipeline was redesigned around capture/judgement separation after a 3-perspective critical review (Claude Opus security/policy, GPT-5.5 architecture, Gemini Flash Lite implementation; Gemini Pro was quota-critical so the verification perspective was routed to Flash Lite). The agreed direction: the capture layer must reliably surface whatever assistant text a child session produced and stop using brittle content heuristics or a `missing_contract` gate to drop/incomplete good answers; the main coordinator judges substance and re-selects/retries. Reviewer-driven correction: "stop validating output" must NOT remove redaction — only content-quality/format gating is removed, while redaction/size-clamp stays in capture. Managed-dispatch beta evidence verification (2026-05-31): durable status reload confirms the **promptAsync mode is evidence-complete** (`workflow-managed-dispatch-retry-4-20260530` has `dispatch_idempotency` reserved + dispatch_completed). The **lane_launch mode is NOT complete**: `workflow-managed-dispatch-launch-20260530` has reserved + dispatch_completed + `lane_lifecycle=running` + a pending_abort_warning but no terminal `task_result`/`task_failed`/terminal lifecycle, and the lane has been `running`→`stalled` for ~12h. Root cause: the managed-dispatch lane_launch path (`dispatchManagedDispatchBetaPromptV1`, adapter ~4433) writes only running `lane_lifecycle` and the `dispatch_completed` idempotency snapshot; it never writes an `agent_task_child_session` record, so the agent-task watchdog (`monitorChildSessionsV1`, which only monitors `agent_task_child_session`) never observes or terminalizes managed-dispatch lanes. Two further prerequisites block a fresh live completion run: (a) the active default managed-dispatch authorization in `~/.config/opencode/opencode.jsonc` expired at `2026-05-30T11:30:00Z` and must be refreshed, and (b) an OpenCode restart + a healthy provider are needed. Open decision before code change: whether to bridge managed-dispatch lanes into the agent-task watchdog (which would let the watchdog nudge/abort a managed-dispatch child session — an authority-surface decision) or add a separate managed-dispatch-specific finalization path.

Resolution (2026-05-31, option B): a managed-dispatch-specific terminal observer was implemented instead of bridging into the agent-task watchdog. `observeAndFinalizeManagedDispatchLaneV1` (managed-dispatch-adapter) reads a launched lane's child session ONCE and writes terminal `task_result` (advisory fields, missing_contract false) + terminal `lane_lifecycle` (`incomplete` with output_ref, or `no_output` when empty); it is idempotent and NEVER nudges, aborts, or enables dispatch/provider/runtime/fallback authority. An opt-in server tool `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_lane_finalize` (durable root + client) exposes it. Unit tests cover terminalize-from-text (asserting zero prompt/abort calls), idempotent skip, and no_output. Full suite 761/761. The expired default managed-dispatch authorization in `~/.config/opencode/opencode.jsonc` was refreshed (`auth-default-managed-dispatch-20260531`, expires `2026-06-02T00:00:00Z`). Remaining for live evidence completion: an OpenCode restart is required to load the rebuilt plugin (new finalize tool + observer code + refreshed auth); after restart the standing real-environment permission allows finalizing the existing stalled orphan lane (`lane-managed-dispatch-launch-20260530`) and running a fresh end-to-end managed-dispatch lane_launch + finalize to close the lane_launch evidence trail.

LIVE COMPLETION (2026-05-31, post-restart): the rebuilt plugin loaded and `flowdesk_managed_dispatch_lane_finalize` was exercised live against the real durable root. Three previously-orphaned managed-dispatch lane_launch lanes were terminalized with zero nudge/abort and all dispatch/provider/fallback authority false: `workflow-managed-dispatch-launch-20260530` → `lane_finalized` (real captured `task_result`, finalization_reason `terminal_marker`, completion `final`); `workflow-managed-dispatch-fresh-retry-20260530` → `lane_finalized` (real captured `task_result`, `terminal_marker`); `workflow-managed-dispatch-model-variant-2-20260530` → `lane_no_output` (no usable text → terminal `no_output` lifecycle, no fabricated result). `flowdesk_status_live` then reported these lanes as `task_result/terminal` (or terminal no_output) with `totalStalledLanes=0`. A full durable scan of all `workflow-managed-dispatch*` sessions confirms **no remaining running-only/orphaned managed-dispatch lane_launch lanes**. Combined with the already-complete promptAsync evidence (reserved + dispatch_completed), the managed-dispatch beta evidence trail is now complete for BOTH modes: promptAsync (reserved+completed idempotency) and lane_launch (reserved+completed idempotency + running→terminal lane_lifecycle + task_result, finalized by the observation-only finalizer). Managed-dispatch beta (P5) lane_launch terminalization is therefore evidence-complete; default Release 1 dispatch authority remains disabled and the finalizer holds no dispatch/fallback authority.

Phase 4 (2026-05-31) added the judgement layer: a new non-authorizing `flowdesk.coordinator_retry_decision.v1` core evidence class (validated, registered in state-paths/session-evidence reload) records the coordinator's substance judgement (success/failure/partial + reason), the advisory inputs it used, and a bounded decision (`accept|retry_reselect|abandon`). A pure `evaluateFlowDeskCoordinatorRetryDecisionV1` policy helper enforces a ≤2 retry cap, mints a fresh attempt id for re-selection, fixes `reselection_basis: "usage_aware_routing"`, and keeps `dispatch_authority_enabled` and `fallback_authority` false so coordinator model re-selection is explicitly pre-launch usage-aware routing, NOT managed fallback authority. The project and global `flowdesk-main.md` prompt contracts were rewritten so lanes are capture-only and the main coordinator judges substance from captured text + advisory metadata, treats only empty/transport failures as lane failure, and on a judged substance failure re-selects a different model and retries via a fresh `flowdesk_agent_task_run` lane (≤2), never `flowdesk_quick_fallback_run`. New core tests cover the evaluator (accept/retry/abandon/cap) and validator (authority rejection, retry_reselect required fields). Full `npm test` is now 759/759. A dedicated MCP writer tool to persist `coordinator_retry_decision` evidence in live runtime remains an optional follow-up; the contract and evaluator are ready for it.

The earlier Phase 1-3 work: (1) `task_result.v1` gained optional advisory fields `finalization_reason` (`terminal_marker|finish_reason|stable_idle|timeout_partial|nudge_exhausted_partial`) and `looks_like_refusal_or_error`, validated and backward-compatible. (2) Capture robustness: `agent-task-output.ts` adds an advisory `looksLikeRefusalOrError` detector and keeps `usableForSynthesis` as transport-only; `agent-task-runner.ts` adds stable-idle early finalization (≥3 unchanged poll cycles, ≥12s unchanged, ≥16 chars, no running tool) so good text returns without an explicit terminal marker, records `finalization_reason`/`looks_like_refusal_or_error`, and sets `missing_contract:false` on the captured-text path (content never causes `task_failed`; only empty capture or transport/launch errors do); `stall-recovery.ts` watchdog records the advisory fields and no longer marks abort-time partial captures as `missing_contract:true`. (3) `workflow-dispatch-tool.ts` no longer converts captured text into `workflow_dispatch_incomplete` via `missing_contract`; it returns `workflow_dispatch_completed` with a `captureAdvisory` block (outputKind/completionStatus/finalizationReason/looksLikeRefusalOrError) for the coordinator to judge. Tests updated accordingly (the former "process-only output as contract-incomplete" server test now asserts completed+advisory; new core validator tests for the advisory fields; new async-lane tests for the refusal/error detector and advisory capture). Verification: `npm run build` and full `npm test` (752/752) pass. Still pending (later phase, per the picked Phase 1-3 scope): main-coordinator judgement + bounded model re-selection/retry semantics (new attempt id, ≤2 retry cap, distinct `coordinator_retry_decision`-style evidence, not managed fallback) and the `flowdesk-main` prompt-contract update ("lane = capture-only; main judges and re-selects"). status-live/TUI already treat task_result with text as terminal/usable; a deeper capture-vs-judgement projection relabel remains optional follow-up.

Each call requires `developerModeAcknowledged=true`, `allowProviderCall=true`, and `allowActualLaneLaunch=true`; accepts exactly one task with concrete agent/model and `contract-task-result-v1`; rejects fallback/reselection, provider switching, controlled write/apply wording, hidden injection, nested OpenCode CLI wording, invalid roles, missing parent session, and missing allow flags before SDK calls; persists `workflow_dispatch_plan` evidence with authority booleans false; launches one lane via `executeFlowDeskAgentTaskV1` using `outputContract: "final_assistant_text"`; reload-verifies terminal `lane_lifecycle` plus `task_result` or `task_failed`; and returns authority that truthfully marks the dev-mode provider/runtime/lane attempt while keeping `realOpenCodeDispatch`, `dispatchAuthorityEnabled`, `defaultRelease1DispatchAuthority`, fallback, hard-chat, and write/tool authority false. Dev/beta controlled write apply was added on 2026-05-27: `packages/core/src/controlled-workspace-file-write.ts` defines reloadable `flowdesk.controlled_workspace_file_write.v1` ledger evidence with disabled provider/runtime/lane/fallback/dispatch/tool/hard-chat authority, and `server.ts` registers `flowdesk_controlled_write_apply` only when `controlledWriteApply.enabled=true`, `controlledWriteApply.devBetaControlledWriteApply=true`, and a durable state root are configured. The tool requires `workflowId`, workspace-relative `targetFilePath`, bounded `replacementText`, `reasonSummary`, `developerModeAcknowledged=true`, bounded `userApprovalRef`, `allowControlledWrite=true`, and either a matching current-content `sha256-...` hash or explicit `allowMissingExpectedHashForDevMode=true`; it rejects absolute/traversal paths, symlink escapes, missing approvals, binary/oversized content, hash mismatch, and forbidden raw/secret markers. It writes by temp-then-rename, preserves existing file mode when practical, reload-verifies durable ledger evidence, and keeps default Release 1 write authority false. Verification passed with `npm run typecheck`, targeted controlled-write/workflow-dispatch and core session-evidence tests, full `npm test` (642/642), `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, and `git diff --check`.

Live dev/beta smoke was completed on 2026-05-27 after restarting OpenCode with the opt-in tools enabled. `workflow-live-dev-dispatch-smoke-20260527b` completed through `flowdesk_workflow_dispatch` after an initial authority-smuggling prompt was correctly blocked; durable status showed one workflow-dispatch plan, one task result, heartbeat/lifecycle evidence, terminal classification, and zero stalled lanes. `workflow-live-controlled-write-smoke-20260527` completed through `flowdesk_controlled_write_apply` after initial invalid-hash/missing-file attempts were correctly blocked; durable status showed one controlled workspace file write ledger and zero stalled lanes. Final verification after removing the artifact passed: `git diff --check`, `npm run typecheck`, full `npm test` (642/642), and `npm run build --workspace @flowdesk/opencode-plugin`.

Async lane orchestration + watchdog nudge/restart was designed and implemented on 2026-05-28. Root cause analysis confirmed that synchronous MCP tool execution blocks the coordinator session while `extractAssistantTextFromResponse` polls the child session — if `session.messages` or `sendNudge` hangs, the entire event loop is occupied and no timer can rescue it. The fix restructures the lane model: `flowdesk_agent_task_run` now supports `asyncMode: true` which returns `{ status: "task_launched", laneId, childSessionId }` immediately after launching the child session, writing `flowdesk.agent_task_child_session.v1` evidence so the watchdog can find it. The watchdog cycle gains a new `monitorChildSessionsV1` phase that polls each running child session, sends `noReply: true` nudges (5s timeout; current default schedule 10s/20s silence), calls `session.abort` after the current abort threshold (30s by default) with 2 nudges exhausted, and writes `task_result`/`task_failed` evidence. `sendNudge` in the blocking path was also upgraded to use `noReply: true` and a 5s hard timeout. A new `agent_task_child_session` evidence class was added to `state-paths.ts` and `session-evidence.ts`. The `model-selection-engine.ts` (usage-weighted model selection per task role) and thin-coordinator design (main agent does ONLY plan/dispatch/synthesize) were added with full test coverage. Design is documented in `docs/conformance/2026-05-28-async-lane-orchestration.md`. All authority flags remain false. Verification passed with full `npm test` (684/684).

The full multi-release roadmap is roughly one quarter complete because Releases 2-4 are intentionally unstarted.

## Release 2/2.5 Implementation Confidence and Uncertainty Policy

Release 2 and Release 2.5 work should proceed incrementally even when some OpenCode runtime conformance details are not yet fully proven. Lack of complete proof is not, by itself, a blocker when the feature can run safely behind explicit opt-in gates, fail-closed checks, durable evidence capture, and clear doctor/status reporting. Uncertain behavior must be documented as an evidence limitation and kept out of default Release 1 authority claims.

### Expected Implementable Areas

1. Durable production-path evidence persistence for usage authority, runtime echo, telemetry correlation, configured verification results, approval decisions, and pre-dispatch audit records is implementable using the existing `session-evidence.ts`, state-store, audit, and validator patterns.
2. A fail-closed production approval state machine is implementable as a core contract before dispatch is enabled; it should default to deny and only later permit conditional dispatch when required evidence is present.
3. Doctor-visible production enablement states are implementable: `disabled`, `blocked`, `configured`, `approved`, and `dispatch-capable` should be represented as diagnostic state, not as implicit dispatch authorization.
4. External auth/provider policy and doctor gating are implementable with conservative provider/model/account/auth-scope binding checks and explicit non-dispatchable diagnostics when evidence is missing or stale.
5. Configured verification integration is implementable by requiring production-path verification config to be read, validated, persisted, and treated as blocking only for the guarded dispatch path.
6. Same-model multi-perspective reviewer separation is implementable at the FlowDesk artifact layer by storing distinct perspective bindings, prompt hashes, lane refs, output refs, and verdict attribution even when the concrete provider-qualified model id is the same.

### Runtime-Conformance Areas To Prove While Building

1. Actual OpenCode `subtask: true` lane lifecycle observability remains uncertain until exercised against the active OpenCode SDK/runtime and recorded as evidence.
2. Injected SDK reviewer lane launch is expected to be feasible, but the exact available runtime echo fields, parent/subtask identifiers, timeout semantics, and failure metadata depend on OpenCode API behavior.
3. Provider/model/account/auth binding can be enforced by FlowDesk policy, but how much of that binding can be independently echoed by OpenCode or external auth plugins remains an evidence question.
4. SDK-scoped cancellation/no-reply controls may be implemented only through first-class OpenCode SDK/plugin surfaces and explicit FlowDesk decisions; this is now complete for `permission.ask`, `session.abort`, and SDK prompt `noReply`. Hook-level `chat.message` blocking/no-reply/cancel authority must remain explicitly unclaimed unless OpenCode exposes a first-class hook boundary. If that hook boundary is not available, FlowDesk may still run SDK-scoped control and steering features while documenting the hook limitation.
5. Runtime telemetry may require FlowDesk-created correlation artifacts if OpenCode does not expose all desired lane observability fields directly.

### Non-Blocking Rule

If a Release 2/2.5 feature works in practice but a conformance proof is incomplete, do not block implementation solely for that reason. Instead, keep the feature opt-in, preserve default Release 1 non-dispatch behavior, store the best available durable evidence, mark the uncertain part in doctor/status/debug output, add negative tests for the safety boundary, and record the exact missing proof in this snapshot or a linked conformance note.

## Active Critical Plan Updates

1. Release 1 must not implement broad OMO-style invisible prefix injection.
2. Chat routing must use conservative, transparent intent handling: leave general chat alone, suggest visibly, route only explicit/high-confidence FlowDesk requests, and block later-gate unsafe FlowDesk routes.
3. Execution-like natural language must stop at confirmation or plan readiness before any guarded dry-run or fake-runtime state change.
4. User-facing copy should avoid internal terms such as `manage`, `non-dispatch`, `adapter`, `pre-spike`, and `fake-runtime` unless a diagnostic/debug surface explicitly needs them.
5. Durable local adapter state must fail closed or surface a blocking error when `.flowdesk` writes fail; command success must not mask failed durable materialization or leave mutated in-memory state ahead of durable state.
6. Pending chat-run confirmations must require exact scoped binding for captured session/source fields and expose a user-completable confirmation path in visible chat steering.
7. Critical review on 2026-05-19 found and the follow-up patch resolved two Release 1 safety blockers: bootstrap durable artifact materialization now validates the full batch before any write, and duplicate chat steering suppression now runs before command-backed state mutation for suppressed non-confirmation cards.
8. Critical review on 2026-05-19 found and the follow-up patch addressed bootstrap installer blockers: installer confirmation now binds target profile, profile root ref, install plan, rollback plan, actor, expiry, and exact typed phrase; command files are rolled back when durable bootstrap artifact writes fail.
9. Critical review on 2026-05-19 found and follow-up patches partially addressed the bootstrap installer profile-binding blocker: `profileRootRef` is now derived from the actual selected `profileRootDir`, the exact typed phrase binds target profile, profile-root ref, confirmation ref, and install plan, direct replay to another profile root is rejected before writes, and successful confirmation refs are consumed once per installer process.
10. The Release 1 bootstrap installer now persists installer confirmations in a lightweight durable ledger under `.flowdesk/bootstrap/confirmations/<confirmationRef>.json`, claims `pending` before bootstrap artifact writes, promotes successful installs to `consumed`, rejects pending/consumed or binding-mismatched ledgers before writes, stores only a typed phrase hash, and fails closed with command rollback if ledger persistence fails. Remaining installer work is CLI/profile wiring and user-facing bootstrap flow integration.
11. Critical review on 2026-05-19 found and follow-up patch resolved durable ledger hardening blockers: installer confirmation now creates a durable `pending` claim before bootstrap artifact writes so incomplete attempts block replay after restart, promotes the ledger to `consumed` only after durable bootstrap artifacts succeed, rejects matching `pending` and `consumed` ledgers before writes, and rejects symlinked or root-escaping confirmation ledger directories.
12. The Release 1 installer now has an explicit `flowdesk-install-release1` CLI/package bin that previews the exact typed approval phrase without writing files, installs only after exact approval, writes portable command files and redacted bootstrap artifacts through the hardened installer library, and reports safe next actions while keeping production registration and provider/runtime dispatch disabled.
13. The OpenCode server plugin now defaults to safe local command-backed tools and visible `chat.message` steering without provider calls, runtime execution, real dispatch, fallback authority, lane launch, or hard chat cancellation/no-reply authority. Explicit `localNonDispatchAdapter: false` plus `naturalLanguageRouting: false` preserves diagnostic-only mode, and `fds1SchemaConversionProbe: true` remains isolated unless local/chat modes are explicitly requested.
14. Release 1 production registration has been promoted only to non-dispatch command-backed registration: schema registry and command manifest minimum tool metadata are production-eligible, the plugin scaffold reports `release1-non-dispatch-command-backed`, readiness checks pass with zero blocked checks, pre-spike sandbox probe registries remain empty/non-authorizing, and tests verify real OpenCode dispatch, provider calls, runtime execution, actual lane launch, fallback authority, and hard chat cancellation/no-reply authority stay disabled.
15. Release 1 packaging/bootstrap smoke evidence was recorded on 2026-05-19: `npm pack --dry-run --json` passes for `@flowdesk/core` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin`, packed files exclude test outputs and `.tsbuildinfo`, the plugin package exposes `flowdesk-install-release1`, and user-facing README/quickstart/manual docs now describe preview/no-write and exact-approval bootstrap flow.
16. The Release 2 managed-dispatch beta core gate layer now exists only as a fail-closed eligibility evaluator in `@flowdesk/core`: it requires managed-dispatch beta policy mode, fresh dispatchable usage, fresh dispatchable provider health, GuardApprovedDispatch, trusted provider/model binding, trusted runtime echo/conformance metadata, sufficient telemetry correlation, durable pre-dispatch audit, configured verification, no fallback or hard-chat authority, and ambiguity quarantine. Release 1 real dispatch remains blocked, and no plugin adapter dispatch is enabled.
17. The Release 2 managed-dispatch beta plugin adapter now exists as a separate opt-in module only: it accepts the core evidence bundle plus a bounded dispatch request, evaluates `evaluateManagedDispatchBetaGuardBoundaryV1` before any SDK call, requires the request model to match Guard approval, uses only injected `client.session.prompt`/`promptAsync`, omits `noReply`/fallback/tool authority, and is covered by fake-client tests. It is not wired into default server tools, so Release 1 remains non-dispatch by default.
18. Release 2 live environment evidence was collected on 2026-05-19: OpenCode 1.14.50 can start a headless server, create a session, and dispatch through `client.session.prompt` to `openai/gpt-5.4-mini-fast` with provider/model identity and expected model text returned. Anthropic OAuth reaches the provider API; direct CLI diagnostics succeed for tested Sonnet/Opus ids, tested Haiku ids return provider model-not-found, pure headless SDK mode fails because it skips the local external Anthropic auth/provider plugin, and non-pure headless SDK mode succeeds for Anthropic Sonnet.
19. 23. Planning update on 2026-05-19: FlowDesk critical review must fan out to every registered highest-tier available reviewer/model lane as extensions of the canonical `reviewer` profile in a planned Release 2.5 or Release 3 entry gate. The model set comes from the active registry and Policy Pack rather than a hard-coded Claude/GPT/Gemini floor. If only one highest-tier model is registered and available, FlowDesk must still perform multi-perspective review by assigning multiple reviewer agents or perspective bindings to that same concrete model. The plan requires explicit registered/available/highest-tier predicates, fan-out budget/concurrency/quota/timeout/retry caps, and a redacted reviewer binding inventory snapshot so the run cannot silently shrink or substitute lower-tier models under pressure. Production orchestration for those lanes and arbitrary agent/model override lanes must use internal OpenCode `subtask: true` lanes or injected SDK/client paths with explicit `agent` and concrete provider-qualified `model` binding, never nested `opencode run`. The capability is not implemented, verified, installed, or release-approved.

No runtime emission path is enabled.

Validators reject unknown labels, forbidden authority-implying states (`enabled`, `active`, `dispatch_ready`, `approved`, `authorized`), and dispatch authority claims. The serialized canonical entry `top_tier_multi_perspective_review_mode=planned` now appears in the `/flowdesk-doctor` `opencode_plugin_compatibility` section refs so users can see the planned reviewer readiness without enabling any runtime authority. Opt-in fake-runtime reviewer lane probe was added on 2026-05-19 in `@flowdesk/core` as a pure-function evaluator `evaluateFlowDeskTopTierReviewerLaneProbeV1` plus typed request/result schemas `flowdesk.top_tier_reviewer_lane_probe.request.v1` and `flowdesk.top_tier_reviewer_lane_probe.result.v1`. The probe supports `subtask_true_command_lane` and `injected_sdk_client` channels, requires `agent_id: "reviewer"`, concrete non-alias provider-qualified model id, perspective from the reviewer perspective enum, six evidence refs (auth/usage/quota/provider_health/runtime_echo/telemetry), `fake_runtime: true`, and `dispatch_authority_enabled: false`. Outcomes are `probe_pass`, `probe_fail_closed` (with failure_label and any one of the evidence slots missing), or `probe_invalid`. Probe results always carry `provider_call_made: false` and `lane_launch_made: false`. A guard test ensures the compiled probe build does not reference `@opencode-ai/sdk`, child process surfaces, or `opencode run`. The probe is not wired into any default server tool, plugin handler, or doctor section; it is exercised only through direct calls in tests/probes.

Planning update on 2026-05-21: multi-model or top-tier multi-perspective review planning must use exact provider-qualified model ids from a redacted same-day availability cache, not abstract labels such as Claude Opus, GPT, or Gemini Pro. Provider calls, runtime execution, actual lane launch, fallback authority, and hard cancel/no-reply authority remained false.

Status correction on 2026-05-22: the SDK-scoped chat/session control slice is considered complete for the surfaces OpenCode currently exposes: `permission.ask` denial, coordinator-issued `session.abort`, and SDK prompt-body `noReply`. Remote write language is also narrowed: controlled local writes for `release_conformance_doc` and `redacted_audit_export` are implemented, while GitHub, connector, storage, database, URL, raw-path, and external ledger writes remain a separate later connector gate.
84. Remote write planning update on 2026-05-22: remote writes are intended to be supported, but only through a dedicated connector profile/gateway because each environment may require different tools, CLIs, MCP servers, APIs, auth scopes, or installation steps. The gate must discover connector capabilities, produce an approved installation or activation plan when required, generate a dry-run write plan, bind content hash/redaction/auth scope/pre-write audit/idempotency, execute only after consumed `external_write` approval, verify a redacted remote ref after the write, and persist only safe refs and summaries. This updates prior wording from permanent remote-write blocking to connector-gate-pending and records that the default design is not direct per-service adapter development. No real remote connector implementation or live remote write has been added yet.
85. Remote write connector gate core contracts were added on 2026-05-22 and recorded in `docs/conformance/2026-05-22-release3-remote-write-connector-gate-contracts.md`: `@flowdesk/core` now exposes connector capability discovery, install/activation plans, dry-run write plans, and execution-readiness evaluation for typed remote targets such as GitHub, HTTP endpoint, cloud storage, database, custom MCP connector, and external ledger entries. The evaluator requires an available connector capability, matching auth scope, matching connector refs, a safe write plan, and a consumed `external_write` approval before reporting readiness, while keeping `remote_write_attempted=false`, `external_write_authority_enabled=false`, and all dispatch/provider/lane/runtime authority disabled. Targeted core verification passed with `npm test --workspace @flowdesk/core -- --test-name-pattern "remote write connector"` and `npm run typecheck --workspace @flowdesk/core`. Post-implementation review lanes were attempted and verdict-only retried but produced no usable deliverables, so they were not counted as approval evidence; direct verification tightened the readiness artifact and schema artifact boolean exposure. `ConnectorProfile` and recipe-ref schemas, skill/command/agent playbook binding, generic connector gateway execution, installation/activation executor, durable remote-write evidence, doctor/status surfaces, and live remote write smoke remain later work.

The tool reloads persisted `runtime_lane_launch_plan` evidence ids, requires explicit `allowActualLaneLaunch=true`, parent session binding, verdict expectations, and consumed `reviewer_fanout` approval, launches the requested reviewer lanes, persists `running` lifecycle evidence, observes matching typed reviewer verdicts, persists `reviewer_verdict` evidence, persists `complete` lifecycle evidence with verdict/output/runtime-echo/telemetry refs, reloads durable evidence, and runs typed verdict acceptance plus durable reviewer-verdict linkage. Regression tests prove the tool is absent by default and missing consumed approval blocks before SDK calls. This closes the explicit product bridge from provider-derived launch-plan evidence to active reviewer execution; the next step is a bounded end-to-end server smoke or command path that invokes provider acquisition -> cache/fan-out/launch-plan materialization -> runtime reviewer execution in one approved flow.
118. Provider acquisition to runtime reviewer execution end-to-end pipeline was added on 2026-05-23 and recorded in `docs/conformance/2026-05-23-provider-acquisition-runtime-reviewer-pipeline.md`: `flowdesk_exact_model_provider_acquisition_live_test` now supports nesting `runtimeReviewerExecution` under `cacheMaterialization.reviewerFanoutPlanning.runtimeLaunchPlanMaterialization`. When all nested opt-in flags are present and an injected `FlowDeskManagedDispatchBetaOpenCodeClientV1`-shaped SDK client is available, a single tool call performs provider acquisition, cache/cache-hit refresh materialization, reviewer fanout planning + persistence, runtime launch-plan materialization, and runtime reviewer execution which persists `reviewer_verdict` and running plus complete `lane_lifecycle` evidence and runs typed verdict acceptance + durable reviewer-verdict linkage. Regression tests prove the chain returns `runtime_reviewer_execution_completed`, `verdicts_accepted`, and `durable_verdicts_accepted` with three linked verdicts and three linked lifecycle refs while keeping default dispatch, fallback, remote-write, and hard-chat authority false; without the nested opt-in the chain stops at launch-plan materialization and no SDK calls run. This closes the bounded user-facing pipeline from active provider availability to durable typed reviewer verdict acceptance; fallback/reselection, remote connector writes, and default dispatch promotion remain separate gates.
119. Active provider-to-reviewer pipeline smoke was recorded on 2026-05-23 in `docs/conformance/2026-05-23-active-provider-to-reviewer-pipeline-smoke.md`: a bounded `opencode serve` plus SDK harness invoked the chained `flowdesk_exact_model_provider_acquisition_live_test` tool once with full nested opt-in, performing a real `openai/gpt-5.4-mini-fast` provider acquisition check, materializing same-day cache plus cache-hit refresh evidence, planning and persisting reviewer fan-out, materializing three runtime launch plans, launching three reviewer lanes, persisting six `lane_lifecycle` records and three `reviewer_verdict` records, and returning `runtime_reviewer_execution_completed`, `verdicts_accepted`, and `durable_verdicts_accepted` with three linked verdicts and three linked lifecycle refs. Durable evidence reload returned `ok=true` with zero blocked entries. The result authority kept `realOpenCodeDispatch`, `providerCall`, `runtimeExecution`, `actualLaneLaunch`, `fallbackAuthority`, `hardCancelOrNoReplyAuthority`, and `dispatchAuthorityEnabled` false; `exactModelProviderAcquisitionRecorded=true` remains a diagnostic flag, not dispatch authority. No `opencode run`, raw token/auth/provider/model payload, transcript, remote write, default dispatch promotion, or fallback authority was used. The remaining product gates are fallback/reselection, remote connector writes, hard-chat authority, and default dispatch promotion.
120. Managed fallback regate server tool plus durable evidence persistence was added on 2026-05-23 and recorded in `docs/conformance/2026-05-23-managed-fallback-regate-server-tool.md`: `flowdesk_managed_fallback_regate` registers only when `managedFallbackRegate.enabled=true`. The tool accepts a `flowdesk.fallback_decision.v1` decision plus a consumed `fallback_reselection` `flowdesk.production_approval_source.v1` approval, invokes `orchestrateFlowDeskManagedFallbackRegateV1`, and returns a redacted summary including orchestrator status, parent/new attempt ids, regate plan state and errors, required fresh evidence ref count, required guard/approval/audit refs, policy/runtime compatibility refs, consumed approval ref, and safe next actions. Authority flags including `automaticFallbackAuthorized`, `providerCall`, `runtimeExecution`, `actualLaneLaunch`, `realOpenCodeDispatch`, `fallbackAuthority`, `hardCancelOrNoReplyAuthority`, and `toolAuthority` always remain false. A new `fallback_regate_plan` session evidence class plus `validateFlowDeskFallbackRegatePlanV1` schema artifact and validator route durable persistence through the same prepare/apply/reload path as other evidence classes. The tool accepts optional `persistRegatePlanEvidence` + `regatePlanEvidenceId` to write the resulting plan as durable evidence; the redacted result reports the persistence status, evidence id, and authority flags. Regression tests prove the tool is absent by default, returns `regate_plan_ready` with three required fresh evidence refs for a valid input, blocks with `blocked_before_regate_plan` when decision/approval are missing or terminal-depth, and persists `state="full_regate_required"` evidence reloadable through `reloadFlowDeskSessionEvidenceV1`. Doctor/status exposure of the persisted regate plan and an active SDK smoke that consumes the plan in a fresh `/flowdesk-run` attempt remain follow-up steps.
121. Quick reviewer run helper, tolerant runtime reviewer execution bridge, hard-chat authority design redesign, and a prompt-driven LLM tool description were recorded on 2026-05-23 in `docs/conformance/2026-05-23-quick-reviewer-run-and-hard-chat-redesign.md` and `docs/USAGE_QUICK_REVIEWER_RUN.md`. `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` is an explicit opt-in tool gated by `quickReviewerRun.enabled=true` plus per-call `developerModeAcknowledged=true` and `allowProviderCall=true`. The tool description guides the assistant LLM to detect review intent and call the tool directly with `developerModeAcknowledged=true` plus `allowProviderCall=true`, treating the plugin-level `quickReviewerRun.enabled=true` opt-in as the single user consent point and explicitly instructing the LLM not to ask for per-call confirmation. A regression test verifies the description contains the `WHEN TO USE` and `WHEN NOT TO USE` sections, the explicit `developerModeAcknowledged=true` plus `allowProviderCall=true` guidance, and the "do not ask the user for extra confirmation" wording, and that it does not mention "paid provider" anywhere. The active OpenCode profile at `~/.config/opencode` was migrated to the local 0.1.1 tarball with the new tool description, and the FlowDesk plugin entry now carries the `quickReviewerRun` options inline as `[name, options]` so the tool registers automatically without any further config changes. The helper auto-generates workflow/attempt/evidence ids from a token-bound timestamp, auto-creates a parent session via the injected SDK client when one is not supplied, persists three runtime launch plans, consumes a synthetic developer-mode `reviewer_fanout` approval, drives the chained reviewer execution bridge, and returns a redacted summary including lane statuses, acceptance status, durable linkage status, and per-lane block reasons. `executeFlowDeskRuntimeReviewerExecutionBridgeV1` was extracted to `runtime-reviewer-execution-bridge.ts` and refactored to be tolerant: each lane outcome is reported in the result array with its own block reason, instead of short-circuiting the whole run on the first failure. Hard-chat authority is repositioned from "intentionally unclaimed pending an OpenCode `chat.message` hook surface" to "explicit SDK-scoped chat control": `session.abort`, prompt `noReply`, and `permission.ask` denial cover the supported cancellation surfaces, `hardCancelOrNoReplyAuthority` remains false as a feature rather than a limitation, and the chat-hook probe continues to record `blocked` for hook-level hard control. A bounded `opencode serve` plus SDK smoke through the new helper returned `quick_reviewer_run_completed`, `verdicts_accepted`, and `durable_verdicts_accepted` with three linked verdicts and three linked lifecycle refs against `openai/gpt-5.4-mini-fast`. A prior smoke produced an incomplete result with a single lane because one perspective's reviewer model did not return a matching typed verdict; the tolerant refactor now reports that as per-lane diagnostic detail and the retry completed cleanly. Tests pass 468/468 across the workspace.

124. Active fallback recovery smoke consuming the persisted regate plan in a fresh `/flowdesk-run` attempt was implemented and recorded in `docs/conformance/2026-05-24-active-fallback-recovery-smoke.md`. The durable pre-call evaluation now requires that if a `fallback_regate_plan` with state `full_regate_required` is present, the fresh dispatch attempt ID must match the plan's `new_attempt_id`, and all required fresh evidence refs from the plan must be loaded in the session evidence. This ensures the fallback recovery adheres to the orchestrated constraints before SDK execution.
125. Gemini provider usage collector reset bucket logic updated on 2026-05-24 to reflect Gemini's shift to 5-hour/1-week reset intervals (matching Claude and OpenAI). `geminiQuotaBucket` now infers the bucket type from the actual reset time: pro models with reset within 24 hours are labeled `gemini-pro-5h`, pro models with reset beyond 24 hours are labeled `gemini-pro-weekly`, flash and flash-lite models continue to use `gemini-flash-daily` and `gemini-flash-lite-daily` respectively. Non-REQUESTS tokenType buckets are now skipped to avoid misinterpreting token-based limits as request limits. The expiredResetBehavior was changed from `stale` to `reset_to_full` (matching the Claude OAuth collector), so an already-reset bucket reports full availability instead of unknown. Four new regression tests verify the 5h/weekly classification, strictest-bucket selection across multiple entries, and TOKENS-type bucket skip behavior. Test count is now 472/472 passing. Live API verification against `https://cloudcode-pa.googleapis.com/v1internal:retrieveUserQuota` confirmed the actual payload shape uses `tokenType: "REQUESTS"` and a single `resetTime` per bucket that can range from sub-24-hour (5-hour resets) to multi-day (weekly resets).

Test count is now 475/475 passing. The portable command routes now cover usage queries (`사용량`, `잔량`, `남은 사용량`, `얼마 남았어`, `쿼터`, `한도`, `리셋`, `사용 가능량`, `토큰 남은`, `크레딧`, plus English `usage`, `quota`, `remaining`, `how much left`, `rate limit`, `reset`, `budget`, `tokens left`), status (`어디까지`, `진행 상황/상태`, `현재 상태`, `작업 상태`), resume (`이어 가`, `재개`, `중단된 거`, `체크포인트`), retry (`다시 시도`, `재시도`, `또 해`), abort (`중단`, `취소`, `멈춰`, `그만`, `작업 취소`), doctor (`진단`, `점검`, `건강 상태`, `설정 확인`, `환경 확인`, `호환성`), and debug export (`디버그`, `로그 내보내`, `버그 정보`, `문제 정보`). The planning, execution-confirmation, explicit-approval, and clarification regexes also now recognize Korean cues (`만들/개발/수정/리팩토/검토/점검/평가`, `돌려/시작/런` adjacent to fake-runtime/dry-run/plan/workflow, `승인/확인/동의/좋아/네/예`, `잘 모르겠/애매/뭐였/뭔가/적당히/대충`). The execution-like regex was tightened so that bare `돌려봐`, `시작해`, `런` only trigger confirmation gating when adjacent to fake-runtime/dry-run/plan/workflow keywords, so phrases like `진단 돌려봐` still route to `/flowdesk-doctor` instead of getting blocked behind an approval prompt. Four new regression tests cover Korean usage, recovery/doctor/debug, review/refactor planning, and clarification cues. Test count is now 479/479 passing. The active OpenCode profile was repacked and force-reinstalled (`@flowdesk/core@0.1.0` and `@flowdesk/opencode-plugin@0.1.1` local tarballs); live verification confirms `사용량 보여줘`, `잔량 얼마야`, `남은 토큰 알려줘`, `오늘 작업 어디까지 진행됐어`, `진단 점검해줘`, `디버그 로그 내보내` all route to the appropriate portable commands instead of falling through as general chat. This complements the description-driven LLM tool discovery for `flowdesk_quick_reviewer_run` and `flowdesk_provider_usage_live`: the chat-intake routing now suggests the matching portable command card for natural-language usage/recovery questions even before the LLM picks up the higher-level tools.
